All Chambers of Commerce Unanimously Oppose the Stamp Tax Law 135

Originally hoped to revise fair and simple methods

Do not heavily tax goods and involve trivial matters

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce believes that the newly revised Stamp Tax Law of the Legislative Yuan violates the principles passed by the Central Political Council and has telegraphed to request correction. Yesterday, the chamber received a telegram from the Changsha Chamber of Commerce, also expressing opposition to the new Stamp Tax Law. The telegrams are recorded as follows:

Telegram from Changsha Chamber of Commerce To the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce: Recently, we sent a telegram to the President of the Legislative Yuan, Sun Jun, stating that the draft Stamp Tax Law proposed by your Yuan stipulates that the tax rate for items such as invoices, account books, and receipts for amounts of three yuan or more to ten yuan is one cent, and one cent is added for every ten yuan thereafter. For items such as stocks, loan agreements, and contracts, the tax is two cents per hundred yuan. The tax on account books is two jiao per year, which is several times to hundreds of times higher than the tax rate in the current provisional regulations promulgated by the Ministry of Finance. The draft bill changes the item-based tax on invoices and other items to a progressive tax, and the progressive level in the draft bill is also changed to one-thousandth. After reading it, we are deeply disturbed. The stamp tax was originally a certificate tax, and the tax rate should be determined based on the strength of the certificate's validity. To take the tax amount of invoices and other items as an example, it directly takes the amount of goods and silver as the standard, which is equivalent to taxing the goods heavily once. This type of certificate is very common in the business community and is not important. Such a regulation seems to contradict the purpose of the certificate tax. Moreover, industries are now in decline and taxes are overlapping. People still feel overwhelmed when paying taxes at the original amount. If it suddenly increases several times, how will they respond? The stamp tax was originally one of the good taxes in various countries, but since its implementation in our country at the end of the Qing Dynasty, more than 20 years ago, although the country's income from this item has increased year by year, the people are complaining. When asked about the hardships of the people, they all regard the stamp tax as the most serious form of harshness. The reason for this is that the staff handling tax affairs cannot be blameless, but the imperfection of the tax law itself is the biggest reason. In the past, the tax rate was divided into categories for the items that should be affixed with stamps, which was extremely trivial. Without thorough research, people often mistakenly fall into the legal net. In addition, the tax rate was inappropriate, and even unimportant certificates were subject to heavy taxes. Merchants in various places were troubled by harsh disturbances, so they repeatedly requested the central government to abolish the regulations and revise fair and simple methods. According to the report, the previous situation is extremely disappointing. We dare to telegraph to your Yuan, and earnestly request that you take into account the people's difficulties and allow the tax rate proposed in the draft bill to be specially reduced based on the current regulations, and another reduced method be formulated in order to be happy to follow and contribute to universalization. We are extremely anxious to await orders, etc. We hope that we will proceed together to the public good. Changsha Chamber of Commerce, Keng.

Reply telegram from Shanghai Chamber of Commerce To the Changsha Chamber of Commerce: We have received the Keng telegram. The Stamp Tax Law has been formally passed by the Yuan. Our chamber believes that it is inconsistent with the principles decided by the Central Political Council last year and has directly telegraphed to the Central Political Council to request correction by virtue of its authority. Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Kou Yuan.

Telegram from the National Federation of Commerce The Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, Lin Shihou, telegraphed the Nanjing Legislative Yuan yesterday, stating that (the title is omitted) the telegram from the Changsha Chamber of Commerce on the Geng day was received, stating (the original telegram is above), etc. With this, we found that the stamp tax passed by your association last year stipulates that those with certificates of validity or rights that are more important or used for a long time should be taxed heavily, and vice versa, taxed lightly. In addition, certificates with frequent behavior often adopt a simple and easy-to-implement fixed-amount tax, and certificates with rare behavior often adopt an easy-to-calculate progressive tax. For example, invoices, account books, receipts, etc., are actually certificates with less important rights, shorter use time, and frequent behavior. Now, although it has been changed to a tax of three yuan, it is calculated progressively, which is even more burdensome. I am afraid that it will be difficult to bear at a time when all industries are declining and business conditions are extremely difficult. It is reasonable to telegraph to your Yuan for verification and approval, and to earnestly request that you quickly reduce the tax in accordance with the principles established last year to facilitate implementation. Sincerely, the Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, Lin Kanghou, Kou Shan.

The Eighth Batch of Expelled Overseas Chinese From Japan Arrived Yesterday 136

The ninth batch will also come to Shanghai today

According to the New Sound Agency, the eighth batch of expelled overseas Chinese from Japan, Jin Zuodun, Xu Chunlang, Lin Qingfa, and three others, arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM on the Japanese ship Ikomamaru from Moji. They stayed at the Yuelai Hotel on the Bund. A reporter from the New Sound Agency met with the overseas Chinese at the hotel yesterday and was told that they were all noodle vendors in Moji. Two months ago, the local police station detained them for no reason and searched them for 94.58 yuan. While in custody, they were subjected to inhuman treatment. They were put on the Ikomamaru to Shanghai a few days ago. However, the ship ticket from Moji to Shanghai only costs 19 yuan. When asked for the remaining funds, they were told that they could collect them from the shipowner after arriving in Shanghai. As a result, they arrived in Shanghai with empty pockets and were unable to collect anything from the shipowner. They originally planned to return to their hometown of Wenzhou, but they need money everywhere, and they cannot do anything without money. Their difficult situation is hard to describe. They deeply hope that the authorities will issue ship tickets and give them some travel expenses so that they will not be impoverished in Shanghai. It is also said that a ninth batch of overseas Chinese will arrive in Shanghai on the Tsukubamaru today.

Fuzhou Wharf Worker Strike: Shanghai Ships Stop Going to Taijiang 137

Change to mooring at Mawei

Yongping Implemented Today

Shanghai to Fuzhou ships have always only gone as far as Mawei. Since the Fujian Provincial Department of Construction dredged the Min River, Shanghai-Fujian liners could directly reach Fuzhou's provincial capital and dock at Taijiang, saving cargo and passengers the trouble of transshipment. Unexpectedly, since Taijiang was opened to navigation, it has caused disputes and fights among dock workers in the two ports, and the situation is becoming increasingly extreme. Today, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Fuzhou liners have stopped going to Taijiang.

Cause of the Labor Dispute: Since Taijiang opened to navigation, regular Shanghai-Fujian liners, such as the China Merchants' Yong'an and Yongping, and the Sanpei's Wanxiang and Jing'an, no longer go to Mawei but instead go directly to Taijiang. Goods destined for Fujian and passengers traveling to Fujian used to be transported by small boats at Mawei, but now they no longer need to be transshipped. However, the dock workers in Mawei, who rely on loading and unloading goods for various commercial ships, now face a situation where hundreds of laborers have no means of livelihood. As a result, Mawei workers and all those traveling with the ships also moved to Taijiang to seek work, but were resisted by the local workers, leading to a major labor dispute.

Conflict Between the Two Sides: Last time the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Shanghai-Fujian liner Yongping arrived in Fuzhou, when it went from Mawei to Taijiang, the Mawei dock workers followed the ship to Nantai, seeking to occupy the loading and unloading work at the Taijiang dock. Unexpectedly, the local dock workers in Taijiang also had a labor union, and considering it a matter of their rights, they refused to allow the workers from Mawei to land and did not allow the Yongping ship to open its hatches and unload cargo. Neither side would give in, and the Taijiang workers organized a crowd to board the ship and engage in a major conflict with the Mawei workers. As a result, the cargo on the Yongping ship was blocked from being unloaded and had to return to Mawei, where the cargo was unloaded and stored in the Mawei warehouse.

Failed Mediation: After this incident, a major labor dispute arose, which not only disrupted public order but also caused stagnation in commercial transportation, which was of great concern. At that time, the Taijiang workers firmly refused to allow the Mawei workers to work in Taijiang, while the Mawei workers, concerned about their livelihood, were determined to follow the ships to Taijiang. The Taijiang labor union then issued a general strike order to deal with the situation. The matter was reported to the Party headquarters by both labor unions, requesting mediation. On the 8th of this month, the Party headquarters mediated and decided that the Taijiang workers would occupy two-thirds of the jobs, and the Mawei workers would occupy one-third. The Taijiang workers expressed satisfaction, but the Mawei workers were unwilling to accept, so the matter remained unresolved, and the labor dispute has not yet been resolved.

Suspension of Navigation to Taijiang: Yesterday, various shipping companies in this city received a telegram from Fuzhou stating that the workers in Taijiang and Mawei had not reached an understanding, the labor dispute had not ended, and the docks in Taijiang were still unable to load and unload cargo. Commercial ships going to Taijiang were likely to be obstructed. Therefore, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Yongping ship has decided not to go to Taijiang and will instead go to Mawei. Cargo destined for Fujian can only be unloaded in Mawei. Before the labor dispute is resolved, Shanghai-Fujian ships will temporarily abandon Nantai.

Changes to Eurasia's Three Routes Schedule 138

Effective October 15th

Eurasia Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Xinjiang, Ping-Guangdong, and Lanzhou-Ningxia routes have changed their flight schedules and abolished the Luoyang station, replacing it with Zhengzhou as a connecting station, effective yesterday. (1) The Shanghai-Xinjiang route's westbound flight departs from Shanghai every Wednesday at 7:10 AM and arrives in Lanzhou every Thursday at 11:30 AM. The eastbound flight departs from Lanzhou every Saturday at 2:00 PM and arrives in Shanghai every Sunday at 2:40 PM. The Lanzhou to Tacheng section has not yet been restored. (2) The Ping-Guangdong route's southbound flight departs from Ping every Sunday and Wednesday at 7:50 AM and arrives in Guangdong every Monday and Thursday at 1:20 PM. The northbound flight departs from Guangdong every Saturday and Tuesday at 10:30 AM and arrives in Ping every Sunday and Wednesday at 4:10 PM. (3) The Lanzhou-Baotou route's northbound flight departs every Thursday from Baotou to Lanzhou, and the southbound flight departs every Friday from Lanzhou to Baotou. However, the Baotou airport still needs repairs, so the route only goes as far as Ningxia. It is estimated that the entire route will be open to navigation around the 30th of this month.

Shipping Administration Bureau Investigates the Truth of the Tongsheng Ship Crashing into a Sailboat 140

The Shanghai Shipping Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications yesterday approved a telegram from Xu Naiguang, chairman of the Zhejiang Shipping Association in Shanghai, stating that according to a letter from Wu Fengfei, manager of the Xu Shenxing sailboat, on October 10th, he loaded 32 round wooden fir barrels from the Zhenchang Lumber Company to be sent to the Dangtu Railway Station. He hired the Hengda New Steamship to go to Wusong together with the Yiyongli sailboat to export the goods. However, when towed to the Jiangmian area of Waigaoqiao in Yangshupu, around 7:30 PM, the Datongxing Company's Tongsheng ship suddenly entered the port at full speed and violently crashed into the Xu Shenxing sailboat from right to left, cutting the hull into three sections, and all the fir was submerged. The total loss, excluding the fir, was estimated to be over 10,000 yuan. The crew members who fell into the water were fortunate to cling to the fir and avoid drowning. They are currently being treated at Shanghai Hospital. After the Tongsheng ship caused the accident, it did not provide assistance and continued to sail. The Gaoqiao branch of the water patrol team heard the alarm and rushed to the scene on the Hengda New Steamship and learned the name of the ship and its affiliated company. The tugboat Hengda New, its driver Chen Sanmao, Xu Shenxing's crew member Yu Peiming, and Yiyonghe's crew member Chen Jiagen were detained for interrogation. It is earnestly requested that your association, considering that one ship supports ten families, that is, dozens of elderly and young people, for their livelihood, promptly submit to the competent authorities to order full compensation and severely punish the drivers who caused the accident. Therefore, this special report is submitted to your bureau for prompt review. After receiving the letter, the Shipping Administration Bureau has contacted the Wusong Fourth Detachment of the Water Patrol Team of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau and the Jianghai Customs to investigate the truth of the incident for review.

Opening of the Third Session of the Freight Transport Training Course on Two Railways 143

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration is holding a freight transport training course to promote cooperation between production, transportation, and sales. The second session of the training course was completed the day before yesterday. Yesterday, the third session of the training course began, with more than 40 trainees from various banks and factories. Director Wu of the bureau personally delivered a speech yesterday. The following is a transcript of his speech: The freight transport training course organized by this bureau originated from the production, transportation, and sales cooperation promoted by this railway. According to the "Outline of Cooperation Methods for Production, Transportation, and Sales at Various Stations along the Line" formulated by this railway, Article 5, "Matters in which this railway engages in cooperation," includes the third item, "Assigning personnel to guide or handle transportation procedures on behalf of places with large-scale production and sales of goods." Now, we are piloting this in Shanghai, and various companies and factories have participated one after another. This is already the third session, which is truly a good sign of cooperation. In this third session, more than ten participants are representatives from various banks. Although the banking industry is not in any of the production, transportation, and sales sectors, the banking industry's handling of import and export bills, warehousing, and other circulation financial facilities are all important and closely related to the production, transportation, and sales sectors, so we feel particularly gratified. Now, I will briefly report on what this railway hopes for. (1) One prerequisite for cooperation is "consistency." All parties participating in cooperation must move towards the same goal, and then great effectiveness can occur. Otherwise, they will be going in opposite directions, and their forces will cancel each other out, or even cause danger. For example, using two locomotives to drive a train, if they are traveling in the same direction, of course, they can increase speed or pulling force. But if they are hung on both ends of a train, one moving forward and the other moving backward, not only will it not move, but it will also cause trouble. Speaking of the production, transportation, and sales cooperation promoted by this railway, broadly speaking, serving society is consistent, and narrowly speaking, seeking to handle matters quickly is also consistent, and seeking to eliminate waste is also consistent. Only under such consistency can there be cooperation. Now, this railway is handling freight transport training from the position of transportation, and the production and sales parties are all participating. This is proof of cooperation. (2) One principle of cooperation is "mutual benefit." Sharing benefits with each other is cooperation. If you rob me and I snatch from you, it becomes competition. Therefore, all parties participating in cooperation must be able to take care of each other's interests and must not be greedy for more benefits for themselves and cause others to suffer losses. For example, this railway is now handling freight transport training, on the one hand, to enable various companies and factories to thoroughly understand the procedures for consigning goods on the railway and then handle the procedures in accordance with the regulations, pay freight at the prescribed rates, save a lot of trouble, and avoid many errors. On the other hand, this railway can also save various explanations when accepting consignment goods and instruct everyone. Saving time is everyone getting benefits. (3) One element of cooperation is "mutual understanding." The so-called knowing the other and knowing yourself, all parties participating in cooperation must have this spirit. For example, this railway is now handling freight transport training, which is telling all its methods to the production and sales parties from the transportation side. The production and sales parties can be said to already know the other. But this railway also needs to know the other, so it also hopes that the production and sales parties, that is, those who are currently participating in the training, will express their opinions on our methods of handling freight transport at any time for reference. Speaking of this point, people can probably be divided into three types. One type is that they do not know themselves, so naturally they have nothing to tell others. Another type is that although they know, they are not willing to tell others, and then they can keep others guessing or have various tricks. There is also a type that although they know, they think it is insignificant and do not need to tell others. Our production, transportation, and sales parties are certainly not the first type of people, but we must not be the last two types of people, and then everyone can be without barriers, and the spirit of cooperation can be even more thoroughly implemented. Finally, there is one more point to say, which is that cooperation must be continuous and must be permanent. Otherwise, if cooperation is cancelled today, it will be ineffective. Therefore, from the perspective of production, transportation, and sales cooperation, after the end of this freight transport training, this railway also hopes that the production and sales parties will have an organization to serve as a hub for constant contact with this railway, that is, permanent cooperation.

Postal Administration Notice Banning the Attachment of Other Letters in Letters 144

The Shanghai Postal Administration issued Notice No. 1169 yesterday, stating: It is verified that letters must not contain letters, notes, or other documents addressed to anyone other than the addressee or anyone living with the addressee. Furthermore, senders must not intentionally mail items abroad or have them mailed abroad, as clearly stipulated in Article 21 of the Postal Regulations and Article 3 of the Final Protocol of the London International Postal Convention. However, it has been found that letters mailed from China to Dalian or Japan have repeatedly been found to contain foreign postage stamps attached, taking the route of Siberia to mail items to Europe. This not only infringes on China's postal rights but also violates the United Postal Regulations and should be stopped immediately. In the future, letters mailed to Dalian or Japan should be opened and inspected by the sender if their circumstances are suspicious before acceptance. If the aforementioned circumstances are found, the sender should immediately pay supplementary postage and affix Chinese postage stamps for direct mailing to the destination. All are hereby notified.

Xue Gansheng and Others Should Be Responsible for the Debts of the Bankrupt Qianzhuang 146

Yesterday's Court Ruling

After the death of the late dye king Xue Baorun, he left behind assets of no less than 10 million yuan. Xue also owned the majority of shares in the Yongjirun and Baokangrun qianzhuang in Wuxi, which were inherited by his four sons, Xue Gansheng, Yansheng, Jiasheng, and Gengsheng. However, due to the extravagance of Gansheng and others, their lavish spending, and their lack of business acumen, the Yongjirun and Baokangrun qianzhuang went bankrupt one after another last year, owing 377,902.97 yuan to 14 households, including the Yongfengzhuang, Yongshengzhuang, Shunkangzhuang, and Yongyuanzhuang, which had dealings with Suzhou. Recently, because the Zhuang and others repeatedly demanded payment from the heirs, the four sons of Xue, but were ignored, they hired two lawyers, Lu Hongyi and others, to file a lawsuit against the four Xue brothers in the Civil Court of the First Special Court for non-payment of debts. The Special Court has held two trials and has now concluded. Fire on Avenue Edward VII Yesterday Morning: As Many as Fourteen People Burned to Death 149

One of them was a pregnant woman, so the total is 15 people.

Most of the corpses were unrecognizable, and only nine people's names were found.

A fire broke out on Avenue Edward VII in the Public Concession around 4:20 AM yesterday morning. Due to the late discovery, 14 men and women were burned to death and seven people were burned, resulting in an unprecedented tragedy. The details are described below.

Packed to the Gills 150

No. 384 East of the Avenue Edward VII Small Vegetable Market is a single-family city house that was rented by Ni Lingsheng to open Ni Shunxing Cotton Shop. The downstairs was used as a shop front, and the other areas, such as the back building, the pavilion room, the second-floor mezzanine, and the kitchen, were divided into seven rooms by Ni Lingsheng and sublet to others. As a result, the single house, including the cotton shop, was occupied by as many as eight families, which can be described as packed to the gills. The neighbor to the left is No. 382, where Yin Deyu opened the Tongchunxiang Candy Shop, and the neighbor to the right is No. 386, where Li Aqing opened the Li Wanli Fruit Shop.

Sudden Fire Alarm 151

Unexpectedly, around 4:20 AM yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out in the cotton pile in the cotton shop's shop front. The tenants in each room were sound asleep, so they did not notice it. As a result, a small fire became a prairie fire. White smoke filled the air, and then the fire spread to the floorboards and upstairs. The tenants upstairs were still sound asleep until the fire was imminent and broke through the roof, spreading to the floors of the neighboring buildings on the left and right. Neighbors shouted and woke them up from their dreams. They tried to escape in a panic, but the ladder had already been burned down, and they were disoriented by the smoke and fire, and fainted one after another. As a result, none of the tenants upstairs escaped, and the shop owner Ni Lingsheng and the shop assistants barely escaped with their lives.

Cries Shook the Sky 152

Fortunately, the neighbors and shop assistants in the surrounding shops were also awakened. Seeing that the fire was out of control, they cried for help and reported to the fire department. The Hongkou and Central fire departments received the news and rushed four fire trucks to put out the fire. But it was already 4:49 AM, and the fire was still raging. Cries of anguish shook the heavens and the earth in the fire pit. The firefighters saw the critical situation and courageously rescued people by raising ladders. While rescuing eight men, women, and children, the floor collapsed downwards. As a result, three men, one boy, three girls, and seven women were all buried in the fire pit, and it was learned that two of the women were pregnant.

The Injured Were Sent to the Hospital 153

It was not until dawn, at 5:35 AM, that the fire gradually died down. The Ni Shunxing Cotton Shop turned into a scorched earth. The floors of the Tongchunxiang and Li Wanli shops were also completely burned down. The firefighters rushed the men who were burned, Ma Shougui, a 24-year-old man from Wuxi, Chen Wencai, a 42-year-old man from Ningbo, and Jiang Yongfa, a 40-year-old man from Changzhou, to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Jiang Yongfa's wife, Pan, 40 years old, was sent to Guangren Hospital for treatment. Two girls, Shi Erbao, 11 years old, Shi Sanbao, 7 years old, and Shi Shen, were also sent to the Shanghai Sanitarium Branch on Bazilu for treatment. Only Shi Shen suffered minor injuries and was discharged immediately. The rest were in critical condition.

Investigation of the Deceased 154

All fourteen male and female corpses that were burned to death were found in the rubble by firefighters after 6 AM. They were shaped like charred wood and had a strange and unpleasant odor. For a time, onlookers gathered, and they were crowded and unable to move. Everyone sighed that the relevant exchange office police station should send a large number of detectives to suppress them. On one hand, they started investigating the names of the corpses. After half a day of investigation, they only found nine people: (1) Zhou Maosheng, (2) Zhou Caichen, (3) Hu Guisheng, (4) Shi Xu, (5) Wang Hong, (6) Zhou Jiang, (7) Jiang Azhen, (8) Jiang Axiang, and (9) Jiang Amao. They used a car to send the corpses to the morgue to request the court to examine them. On one hand, they investigated the cause of the fire and detained the shop owner Ni Lingsheng for further investigation. However, according to neighbors, it was feared that it was caused by a cigarette butt left in the cotton pile. In addition, the weather suddenly turned cold last night, and everyone was sound asleep. At the same time, the discovery was delayed, resulting in this disaster, which is also very tragic.

Englishman Killed in Car Accident 156

First Hit a Pedestrian, Then He Also Fell Out of the Car and Suffered Serious Injuries

The injured pedestrian did not die, but the driver died of serious injuries.

An Englishman, a Scotsman named McDougall, came to Shanghai from England three months ago and worked in the accounting department of the Shanghai Electric Tramway Company. He lived at No. 14, Lane 188, Avenue Albert in the French Concession. Because the journey was long and inconvenient, he bought a motorcycle for transportation. Its number was 2018. Around 1:30 PM the day before yesterday, Dugal was driving his car east of Jing'an Temple Road, Carter Road, and west of Tongfu Road, from east to west. At that time, Du Decheng, a native of Yangzhou, who was the director of the cashier's department of the Wuxi Zhongnan Bank, also known as Du Shangzhai, 50 years old, crossed the road, causing the Westerner to be unable to avoid it in time. The man and the car collided. Du Decheng was knocked down, and his head and legs were injured. The Westerner also fell from the car due to the sudden stop, and his head was severely injured, with blood gushing out. Yin Pu, number 1225, who was on duty at the station, saw it and sent the injured Westerner to Hong'en Hospital, and Du Decheng was sent to the Red Cross on Hague Road for treatment. However, the Westerner Dugal died shortly after due to his serious injuries. Afterwards, the Xinzha Police Station immediately ordered Chinese and Western detectives to conduct a detailed investigation. Du Decheng was indeed negligent in this case, so yesterday morning, the police station took him from the hospital and sent him to the Criminal Court No. 8 of the First Special Court, requesting permission to detain him for investigation in accordance with Article 49 of the Criminal Procedure Law. Du Decheng hired lawyer E Sen to defend him in court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the case, saying that when the accident occurred, the Westerner Neil, Webber, and Yin Pu, number 325, witnessed it. According to the two Westerners' statements to Yin Pu, the fault in this case lies entirely with Du Decheng, because he did not pay attention to the passing vehicles at the time and suddenly rushed out from the side of the road, resulting in the accident. Now, permission is requested to temporarily detain Du because the victimized Westerner will be sent to Hong'en Hospital by the British Consulate this afternoon for an examination, and Du must also be brought to the case for questioning. Yin Pu, number 325, testified, "I was on duty at that place yesterday. When the accident happened, I raised my hand to stop north-south traffic and allow east-west vehicles to pass. The Westerner's motorcycle was the last vehicle, traveling from east to west. At that time, the petitioner suddenly rushed out from the south and walked north, crossing the road. Because he did not pay attention to the vehicles in the road and was only a foot away from the Westerner's car, he could not avoid it, and the motorcycle crashed into Du's body and fell to the ground. The Westerner also fell from the car due to the urgency of stopping the car." Du Decheng confessed, "I have been the director of the cashier's department of the Wuxi Zhongnan Bank. I came to Shanghai this time on the 13th of this month from Jiangbei and stayed at the Kaitai Hotel on Tianjin Road. Yesterday afternoon, when I was returning from visiting friends on Weihaiwei Road, I passed through the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Tongfu Road. This road is a north-south straight road. I was crossing the road from west to east. At that time, there were very few vehicles passing by, and I did not see the Indian raising his hand to stop me. When I was about to reach the pedestrian road opposite, the Westerner's motorcycle suddenly drove from the front. Because his car was traveling too fast and I did not hear the horn, I was hit head-on, injuring my head and legs. The Westerner also fell from the car," Lawyer E Sen argued that according to today's court hearing, Du Decheng was not at fault, and he himself was seriously injured and urgently needed medical treatment. He cannot be detained for no reason and suffer. Therefore, he requested permission to post bail for medical treatment. Judge Liu Yugui examined the confession and ordered that the case be adjourned, and Du Decheng was allowed to post a 500-yuan bail and be responsible for appearing whenever summoned for questioning.

The West Face Dye Industry Guild Refutes Slander on Tong Ren He 157

Letter to D. Delfs & Co.

Regarding the case of Tong Ren He Dye Shop, located at No. 80, Rue de la République, French Concession, being accused of trademark infringement by D. Delfs & Co., as reported in this newspaper, the shop has since negotiated with D. Delfs & Co. The company has acknowledged the misunderstanding and has stated in a letter that they are taking steps to withdraw the accusation. However, Xu Chengdong, the manager of Tong Ren He, felt unjustly accused and complained to the Shanghai West Face Dye Industry Guild, requesting assistance. The guild convened a general meeting of all members, discussed the matter, and resolved to send a letter to D. Delfs & Co., urging them to follow through on their letter and take responsibility for withdrawing the accusation. The original letter is as follows:

To Whom It May Concern: According to our member, Tong Ren He Dye Shop, we have a contract to distribute D. Delfs & Co.'s "Candle Red" with the six-tael "Longevity Star" trademark. We have also registered the use of the "Longevity Star" trademark with the Trademark Bureau. The back of the can features a red candle, symbolizing that the raw material is used for candle red. Unexpectedly, D. Delfs & Co. nitpicked and hastily claimed that we were imitating their "Three Stars" trademark. They falsely reported it to the French police, who sent detectives to search our shop. Under the guidance of a Westerner from D. Delfs & Co., they ransacked the place and forbade us from making any noise. It was later found that the "Longevity Star Candle Red" sold by our shop was all original goods under the distribution contract signed with D. Delfs & Co. The truth came to light, and they admitted their mistake, stating in a letter that they "have taken steps to withdraw the accusation from the police." However, our shop's business reputation has suffered greatly. If justice is not upheld in this matter, the consequences will be unimaginable. We request that you provide the original letter from D. Delfs & Co. to the guild. Based on this, whether or not there is trademark infringement depends on whether the goods distributed under the signed contract are counterfeit. Now that it has been verified that they are original goods, there is no apparent act of counterfeiting. They have admitted their mistake and have taken steps to withdraw the accusation, which we now understand. Given these circumstances, the actions taken by your company beforehand were too rash and have aroused resentment among our industry colleagues. Since this case is a public prosecution, it falls under the jurisdiction of the police. Since your company has stated that it will take steps to withdraw the accusation, you should take responsibility for handling the matter. Furthermore, many of our guild members are long-standing customers of your company in China, and the basic business dealings are a direct benefit. However, you often make a mountain out of a molehill on minor trademark issues, disregarding your business relationships and antagonizing your customers. This attitude is extremely detrimental to maintaining business relations and should be avoided. This case was brought up for discussion at the members' meeting on the ninth of this month, and it was decided that "D. Delfs & Co. should be more careful in the future regarding the trademarks used by our colleagues to avoid disputes and damage to business relations, and a letter of advice should be sent." Accordingly, we hereby inform you that in the future, when trademark issues arise with our colleagues, you must be careful to avoid harming business relationships. We hope for your prompt reply. Sincerely, The Shanghai West Face Dye Industry Guild.

Modern Wife Sues 158

Unwilling to Live with Old-fashioned Parents-in-Law

The Court Has Already Attempted Mediation Twice

Tu Guiliang, a native of Ningbo, is 28 years old and a graduate of the YMCA school of St. John's University. His father, Tu Yonggui, is nearly sixty and runs the Xingchang Foreign Goods Store at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Shandong Road. In 1926, through a matchmaker, he married Dai Miaozhen, a graduate of the McTyeire School for Girls, whose father, Dai Ziming, was a leather goods merchant (now deceased). Since their marriage, Tu and Dai have had a good relationship and have two sons and four daughters. The fourth boy died young; the rest are still living. The family lives on the third floor of the Xingchang store, where Tu's parents also reside. Tu Yonggui provides his daughter-in-law with a monthly allowance of fifty yuan. However, Dai is a so-called "modern woman" who dresses fashionably and has extensive social contacts, frequenting dance halls, theaters, and other entertainment venues. In the summer, she is particularly fond of swimming. The Tu family is entirely old-fashioned. Her parents-in-law disapproved of their daughter-in-law going to dance halls and swimming pools, and swimming and dancing with men, considering it improper. They tried to stop her, but Dai believed that these were legitimate social activities and that as long as there was no inappropriate behavior, no one could stop her. This led to frequent arguments. On August 27th of this year, a conflict arose which led to physical violence, and they ended up fighting at the police station. Tu Guiliang mediated to prevent a lawsuit, and they returned home together. However, on September 11th, Dai Miaozhen took one daughter, along with her jewelry, and left without returning. She also hired attorney Jiang Yiping to send a letter to Tu, requesting to live separately from her parents-in-law and attaching various conditions. After receiving the letter, Tu hired attorney Chen Chou to file a petition with the mediation office of the First Special District Court, requesting a summons for mediation to live together and to bring back the eldest daughter, Yuanyuan, and the gold jewelry and clothing that had been taken away. At the same time, Dai also hired attorney Jiang to file a petition for mediation to live with her husband but separately from her parents-in-law. One mediation had already been held. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Tao Dejun held another hearing for mediation. According to attorney Chen, the female side requested 400-500 yuan per month for living expenses after separation, and that a large sum of money be prepared as a security deposit for living expenses, guaranteeing at least two years' worth of expenses. She also required that the gold jewelry that had been pawned be redeemed. However, Tu Guiliang's financial power was entirely in his father's hands, and due to the decline in business, it was impossible to afford it. At most, he could pay 100 yuan per month for living expenses after separation and hoped that the woman could return home to live together. The female side stated that the minimum requirement was 200 yuan per month. The court immediately mediated with a compromise of 150 yuan, but both sides were unwilling to agree and requested a postponement to persuade each other further to avoid going to extremes. The court approved the request and adjourned the hearing to a later date.

Organized by a Stable Foreman

The Organizer and Gamblers Sentenced Separately

Liu Yaying and Ji Cunyi, Chinese detectives of the Chengdu Road Police Station, learned that a cricket fighting venue had been organized at No. 56, Yongqing Lane, Dagu Road, with large sums of money at stake. Red Swastika Society Hosts Banquet for Leaders of National Orphanages 160

Red Swastika Society Hosts Banquet for Orphanage Leaders (Photo by Wang Kai) 161

The representatives of the World Red Swastika Society China Headquarters and various branches, including Xiong Xiling, Cheng Miaokong, Zhang Lanping, Han Shichang, Luo Shanda, Sun Huizhou, Li Jingji, Ma Haifeng, Zhou Genjing, and Li Daoyuan, held a public banquet for the leaders of national orphanages at 6 PM on the 14th at the society's office in Zhonghe Village, Xibushi Road. More than a hundred people attended, including Xu Junren, Qu Wenliu, Zhu Ziqiao, Zhao Jinqing, Lu Bohong, Chen Tiesheng, Chen Peide, Weng Guoxun, and various representatives. President Xiong Xiling gave a welcoming speech, stating that he was representing the entire Red Swastika Society in extending a sincere welcome to the leaders of national orphanages. Although the society is a member of the charitable organizations, all of its work is closely related to the orphanage work. The situation of orphanage education in various provinces and branches has been reported at the meeting. He always had a good relationship with the representatives in promoting orphanage work. He regretted being unable to attend due to illness. However, the results of the meeting showed that everyone was committed to promoting the progress of orphanage work and had a complete plan, like kind fathers and mothers of the children. The society members deeply admired this. He hoped that everyone would provide guidance to the society at any time and would cooperate in material and spiritual matters in the future. He toasted to everyone's health. President Zhang Lanping then gave a speech, stating that all countries in the world are now committed to war preparations, and a deadly atmosphere fills the earth. The work of managing orphanages is to seek the way of life, nurture, and education, to seek a glimmer of hope in the midst of death. He hoped that everyone would work together to promote the way of life, awaken the spirit of mutual assistance and love among mankind, and eliminate the ominous atmosphere of death in the world. The leaders jointly elected Chen Peide, representative of the Sichuan Provincial Department of Civil Affairs, and Chen Tiesheng, Director-General of the China Orphanage Association, to give speeches expressing their gratitude. The banquet ended at 8 PM with the guests and hosts in good spirits. During the banquet, Tao, a representative of the Fuyu Industrial and Children's Hospital, reported on the progress of the hospital, which has now raised more than 1,000 children. He hoped that the representatives would visit the hospital on Yulin Road for guidance. More than 80 people signed up on the spot and were scheduled to visit at 9 AM the next day.

Industrial and Occupational Accident Statistics for the Public Concession Last Month 163

According to reports obtained by the Public Works Department, a total of 176 industrial and occupational accidents occurred in the Concession in September (178 in August). Eight people died and 152 were injured. The causes of the accidents are generally clear. 105 of them have been investigated and discussed with the factories.

Classifying the causes of the accidents, 49 were due to electrically powered machinery, including 16 involving belts and pulleys, 9 involving presses, and 9 involving shafts and cylinders. However, only a few people were seriously injured in machinery accidents, and fortunately no one died. However, three people died from electrical accidents. 46 people were injured by falling objects, one of whom died. 25 people were injured by falls, two of whom died. Eight people were burned by hot materials and molten liquids.

Analyzing by occupation, the metal and machinery industry had the most accidents, with 39 people injured and one death. Next was the construction industry with 30 people injured and two deaths, the textile industry with 23 people injured, the clothing industry with 11 people injured and one death, the food and beverage industry with 14 people injured and one death, the printing industry with 13 people injured and one death, and the transportation industry with 16 people injured and two deaths. Public Works Department Information Office, October 15, 1934.

Postal Inspector Wounded by Thugs 166

Feng Zhiqing, 31 years old, from Nanjing, has been working as an inspector on the third floor of the Sichuan Road, Baidu Bridge Post Office. He is known for his conscientiousness in his work, which has led to resentment from criminals. Unexpectedly, at around 4:05 AM yesterday morning, while Feng was sleeping soundly in the inspector's room, a thug suddenly came and struck Feng's head with an axe. When Feng woke up in pain and called for help, his fellow police officers arrived, but the assailant had disappeared. Feng was taken to Renji Hospital by inspector Wen Zhong for treatment. It is reported that his injuries are very serious and his life is in danger. Feng previously served as an inspector at the Third Sub-station of the Sixth District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau and was transferred to his current position on August 20, 1932.

Fake Recruitment Employs Copper Medals to Collect Money, Large Numbers of Coolies Deceived 168

At around 10 PM the night before, Gao Minglong, a police officer at the Zhongxing Road Police Station of the Xinzha Public Security Bureau, brought Xu Yuanji to the station after being apprehended by Shen Xintai. Shen Xintai accused Xu Yuanji, 36 years old, from Dongyang County, Zhejiang Province, currently residing at No. 58 Zhangjiabang, Jumen Road, Nanshi, and working as a carpenter, of falsely claiming that someone had invested a large sum of money to contract a mine in Dongyang and Yiwu counties in Zhejiang Province and was in urgent need of excavation. Therefore, he was sent to Shanghai to recruit a large number of miners. Anyone willing to work must obtain a copper medal (the copper medal is shaped like a large copper coin with the words "Dong Cheng" cast on it). Each medal costs three yuan. After obtaining the copper medal, one can go to the mining site to report for work. Therefore, many people signed up for the job. The individual was subcontracted to recruit workers by Xu and was defrauded of more than 900 yuan. Later, Xu disappeared without a trace. He was spotted on Yongxing Road, Yuyingtang Road, the other night and was taken into custody. Xu Yuanji confessed that he was 41 years old, from Yuyao, had no fixed address, and (46 remaining copper medals were found on his body). In November of the lunar calendar last year, a man named Jin Meilan came to Shanghai with him to contract the recruitment of workers. Unexpectedly, the mining failed, and Shen Xintai was also a subcontracted labor contractor. He owed Shen more than 400 yuan, so he took him into custody today. He admitted that he issued all the copper medals. After the interrogating officer verified the confession, he ordered the case to be submitted to the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau Zhabei Branch and transferred to the Shanghai Local Court for interrogation on suspicion of fraud.

The Issuance Department of the China Industrial Bank maintains its reserves completely separate from the funds of the Business Department to ensure full reserves. Herewith, the amount of issuance reserves as of October 13, Year 23 is announced as follows: The total amount of banknotes issued is 35,543,013 yuan, which includes 18,243,013 yuan issued by this bank, 9,150,000 yuan issued by affiliated banks, and 8,150,000 yuan taken by branches and sub-branches. Apart from the portions taken by each branch and sub-branch being inspected according to the original methods, this inspection covered 27,393,013 yuan of banknotes issued by this bank and its affiliated banks. The reserve funds for these banknotes issued by this bank and its affiliated banks total 27,393,013 yuan, which includes 16,789,088.40 yuan in cash reserves and 10,603,924.60 yuan in guarantee reserves. The above two items show that the cash reserves account for over 60%, and the guarantee reserves account for over 40%, and all amounts were verified to be correct without any discrepancies. Inspector: Zhang Yi Yan, accountant at the Zhengze Certified Public Accountants Firm.

▲ Mexican Specialty Jumping Beans. The Baoji Wine and Food Company, located at 360 Zhapu Road next to the Hongkou Grand Theater, has received a rare and mysterious jumping bean from Mexico. The beans are triangular in shape and have an oval bottom, similar to roasted coffee beans. They prefer warmth and move with extraordinary agility when placed under electric lights, jumping back and forth like butterflies flitting among flowers. They can even race. Mexicans often use these jumping beans to bet money on races. Several jumping beans are designated to different people, and then placed at the same starting point. The first to reach the designated line wins. Currently, Mr. Shao Bao-san, the manager of the company, in order to promote research by all sectors, has not only put these jumping beans on public display, but has also invited a Westerner named Kao Si-Tuo to be stationed to explain them, so that all sectors of society can study and explore them. He is also willing to give them away (the number is limited to 5,000 beans). Anyone who purchases Javanese white sugar for one yuan or more, or a can of Javanese coffee, will receive one mysterious jumping bean as a gift, starting from today.

Special Article

The Ministry of Finance's Increase in Silver Export Tax 176

— Cheng Shao-de

The issue of rising silver prices has become increasingly acute since the passage of the U.S. Silver Purchase Act in June of this year. The London and New York silver markets have gradually strengthened since June 22. By early July, the average London silver market had increased by one and a half pence per ounce, and the New York silver market had risen from around 45 cents to over 46 cents. Observe the table below:

Date London Silver Market New York Silver Market

June

20th 19 and 7/8 45

21st 19 and 5/16 45 and 1/8

22nd 20 and 1/16 45 and 1/8

23rd 20 and 5/16 45 and 1/4

25th 20 and 3/8 45 and 1/4

26th 20 and 5/16 45 and 1/4

27th 20 and 7/16 45 and 5/8

28th 20 and 3/4 46

29th 21 and 1/8 46 and 1/4

30th 21 46 and 1/4

Since July, the London silver market has generally remained around 21 pence. At the same time, the Shanghai foreign exchange rates quoted for London were also lower than the silver parity between London and Shanghai. In the past, the extent of the discount was very limited, at most 0.125 or 0.25 pence lower than the Sino-British exchange rate parity. Now, the extent of the discount is becoming more and more severe. For example, on August 1, the Sino-British parity should have been 17.125 pence, but the HSBC quote was only 16 pence, a discount of as much as 1.125 pence. On August 21, the difference was even greater, reaching 1.875 pence. As such, on August 21, the Shanghai market could purchase one yuan for only one shilling, four pence, and three-seventy-five. If it were sold in the London market on the same day, one could obtain one shilling, six pence, and two-five of British currency. In one transaction, a profit of 1.875 pence could be made per Shanghai silver dollar. In other words, buying and selling 100 million silver dollars could yield a profit of 187,500,000 pence, which, at the value of that time, could yield a profit of about 11 million yuan. No wonder there has been a large outflow of silver from Shanghai in the past two months. At the end of July this year, Shanghai's silver reserves were 530,402,000 yuan. By the end of August, they had dropped to 483,740,000 yuan. By the end of September, they had changed to 445,363,000 yuan. Since October, the amount of silver flowing out of Shanghai in two weeks has reached 26,850,000 yuan. Therefore, since the U.S. Silver Purchase Act was approved by the U.S. President on June 20, the silver market has been trending stronger. After the U.S. announced its silver nationalization policy on August 9, the situation took a turn for the worse. Last week, the London silver market even rose to 24 pence per ounce. For example, on October 14, the near-term price was 24 pence, 4375, and the forward price was 24 pence, 5625. Accordingly, the Shanghai-London foreign exchange parity should be one shilling, eight pence, and 5625. However, on that day, the Central Bank's quoted London telegraphic transfer rate was one shilling, six pence, and one-two-five, while HSBC's quoted rate was only one shilling and six pence. Even when calculating the forward rate, the quoted price was still very different from the parity. Therefore, from the various technical points mentioned above, the outflow of silver from our country is unavoidable. At such a critical juncture, the government should adopt no more than two main policies: first, directly declare a ban on silver exports; second, levy a silver export tax to reduce the difference in silver speculation profits. However, for our country, which is a silver standard country, the former is tantamount to directly abandoning half of the silver standard. Regarding the various financial measures after the prohibition of silver exports, given our environmental circumstances, we may not be allowed. Therefore, we can only take the second method of levying a silver export tax. In the past, the silver export tax was only 2.5%. However, according to our calculations, the difference between the London silver market and Shanghai silver prices has been about 10% in the past two months. As such, after deducting 2.5% for transportation costs, 2.5% for tariffs, there is still a profit of about 5% for shipping silver from Shanghai to London. As of the last two weeks of this month, the London silver market has been even stronger, and the profit from shipping silver from Shanghai to London has also increased compared to the past. Therefore, silver exports have also been unleashed and cannot be stopped. The Ministry of Finance formally announced yesterday morning (the 15th) that it would raise the silver export tax to 10%, which is appropriate. Its regulations for determining the silver export tax rate are as follows: (1) Silver standard currency will be subject to an export tax of 10%, deducting the minting fee of 2.25%, resulting in a net tax of 7.75%. (2) Large bars of treasure silver and other types of silver will be subject to an additional tax of 7.75%, combined with the original 2.5%, for a total of 10%. (3) If the London silver price converted to the Shanghai exchange rate differs from the exchange rate determined by the Central Bank on that day, and the amount is still insufficient after paying the above export tax, a balancing tax should be levied according to the insufficient amount. At the same time, the Central Bank also announced that "Starting from October 15 of this year, this bank will comply with the government's instructions on levying taxes on silver exports and will determine the market price of all calculated differences between the London silver price and the Shanghai telegraphic transfer to London in shillings at 11:30 a.m. every business day and notify the customs so that they can calculate accordingly." As such, based on the parity and foreign exchange rates between Shanghai and London in recent days, the 75% tax rate will reduce the speculation of transporting silver to London or New York. At the same time, the so-called balancing tax will be levied to stop the practice of transporting silver for profit based on price differences. Given the environment in which our country finds itself today, the strategy adopted for the outflow of silver in all financial organizations is appropriate. Finance Minister Kong's two major financial measures recently are: first, to prohibit the speculation of gold standard, so that the settlement price of gold standard will be based on the customs silver price of the Central Bank, so that the sovereignty of the settlement price of the largest gold standard market in the Far East will not depend on the foreign exchange market, but will consolidate its barriers; second, to resolutely increase the silver export tax and restrict the speculative export of silver, which is of great importance to the stability of our country's finance. Consolidating the financial foundation and striving for the development of the national economy are appropriate measures.

Exclusive Item

The Awakening of National Self-Reliance and Revival (Part 3) 177

— Draft by Zhang Yuan-ruo

丨At the Chinese Vocational Education Society 丨

7. Comparison of Self-Reliance and Various Doctrines. A detailed and specialized study should be conducted separately to compare self-reliance and various doctrines. Here, the most superficial method will be used for explanation.

(1) Comparison of Self-Reliance and Liberalism丨Liberalism is based on rights, while self-reliance is based on duties and responsibilities. In the West, property rights are called freedom of property. In law, whatever is freedom is the meaning of rights. Self-reliance is anti-freedom and does not advocate that an individual takes rights too seriously. My legal thought is based on obligations (see my "Modern Constitutionalism," Zhonghua, and "Outline of Modern Legal System," Commercial Press). Therefore, the spirit of my self-reliance is also consistent. (2) Comparison of Individualism and Self-Reliance丨Individualism also has its advantages and disadvantages. Greek thought advocates self-awareness, which is an advantage of individualism. Now, because it is too permissive, it has developed serious morbidities. Self-reliance is produced to correct this morbidity. (3) Comparison of Self-Reliance and Socialism丨Self-reliance differs from extreme socialism in that socialism obliterates individuality. Everything is social, and there is no development of individuality. In the past, Russia practiced extreme socialism, and as a result, individuality could not develop, industry stagnated, and production decreased. Therefore, it changed to the New Economic Policy. Although self-reliance advocates that society and the country are the foundation, it also emphasizes self-awareness. The development of extreme socialism should also be corrected. (4) Comparison of Self-Reliance and Democracy丨The characteristic of democracy lies in the average development of national individuality. It does not mean that a republic with a parliament can be called a democratic country. The characteristic of democracy can be said to be the same as self-reliance, because self-reliance also wants to enable each citizen to develop his or her strengths. However, the difference is that democracy is based on liberalism, and self-reliance does not allow individuals to have absolute freedom. One must be able to fulfill one's obligations to the state and society before one can enjoy freedom. (5) Comparison of Self-Reliance and Fascism丨Fascism is a kind of activism. I sympathize with this point, because in real time and space, everything should be done vigorously. However, my self-reliance is the way of the king, and it differs from the spirit of fascism. (6) Comparison of Self-Reliance and Soldarisme丨Soldarisme calls for Soldarisme. My brother believes very much in this doctrine. The foundation of my brother's legal studies is completely built on Soldarisme. It divides society into two phenomena and has two kinds of relationships at the same time: (A) Seeking simultaneous social solidarity: Solidarite Por Similitude; (B) Social solidarity of division of labor: Solidarite por Division du tirvtal. The observation of social phenomena is not biased towards the individual, nor is it biased towards society, but is just right, like the doctrine of Confucius. In the social relationship of seeking common ground, we should work hard for society. In the social relationship of division of labor, we should do our best, develop our strengths, and be loyal to our duties. Therefore, Soldarisme can be said to be the middle way to adjust the two thoughts of individual liberalism and extreme socialism. Although self-reliance cannot be said to be absolutely the same as it, in terms of the spirit of thought, it can be said to be consistent with each other.

8. Advantages and Functions of Self-Reliance. Where are the advantages of self-reliance, and what are its uses? We can see from the comparison of self-reliance with various doctrines that it eliminates the shortcomings of each doctrine and has the advantages of each doctrine. It is not speculative, and at the same time, it does not surrender to any faction of thought. It takes the strengths of various philosophical thoughts and abandons their shortcomings. Therefore, self-reliance can be said to be the culmination of various doctrines and various philosophical thoughts, and can be regarded as the most perfect doctrine in modern times. Self-reliance is so good in theory, but is it consistent with the current society? There are many morbidities in Chinese society today, and the reason why self-reliance is so valuable is that it can correct these many morbidities one by one. For example, the diseases of the Chinese people lie in empty talk, vanity, opportunism, luck, blaming others, dependence, laziness, inertia, fear of difficulty, complacency, baseness, power struggles, selfishness, indulgence, decadence, and consumption. Self-reliance is mainly about action, practicality, hard work, effort, self-blame, self-seeking, diligence, courage, enterprise, hard work, perseverance, loyalty, struggle, perseverance, and production. The morbidities of the general public can be corrected by self-reliance. I believe that self-reliance is really the most applicable to our country and the doctrine that can best inspire the national spirit. It is not only complete in theory.

Free Talk

Popular Editions of Books 182

— Guan Jingzhi

Walking along the road, I often see rows of stores displaying their merchandise in large glass windows. All kinds of goods are arranged neatly, sometimes very novel. The window dressing art of stores has improved a lot recently.

However, in the middle of a row of competing and dazzling large glass windows, I have also often seen shops that have closed down, looking like they have lost an eye. This is especially striking at night when the red neon lights make people's eyes ache. It is as if a "recession" sign has been inserted into the seemingly prosperous market.

However, I don't know when, many temporary book stalls have been added in front of these closed shops that look like they have lost an eye. Most of them use the window sills as bookshelves, displaying pirated old novels, such as "Dream of the Red Chamber," "Water Margin," "Romance of the Three Kingdoms," "The Scholars," "The Scarlet Robe," "Biography of Yue Fei," "Family Letters of Zeng Wenzhenggong," "Letters from Qiushui Xuan," "The Peach Blossom Fan," "Six Records of a Floating Life," and even stone-printed calligraphy books like those by Prince Cheng.

These books mostly have new-style punctuation and paragraphs, are printed on newspaper, and have kraft paper covers. The list price is not that low, but the selling price is "let go" to the point that people can hardly believe it: usually 10% off the discount. You can get a copy of "Romance of the Three Kingdoms" for three or four mao.

This did not exist before! The prevalence of such "popular editions" on the one hand indicates the wide demand, but on the other hand, it may also reflect the struggle of the book industry in the tide of "recession," right? I often think this way.

In any case, the popularity of "popular editions" is always a good thing. In today's situation where the wallets of book buyers are getting thinner and thinner, "popular editions" are always beneficial to "culture."

I have had several transactions with these small book stalls. What I admire is that the printing of these "popular editions" is not bad. Old vernacular novels such as "Romance of the Three Kingdoms" hardly have any typos, and the punctuation is mostly correct. However, the classical "A New Account of Tales of the World" has more typos. This is not surprising. In such a "recession" era, for the sake of cost, these "popular editions" certainly cannot hire "experts" to proofread!

Recently, the application of "popular editions" has expanded to very "hardcore" major books. First, there were advertisements for zinc-plate reduced editions of the "Twenty-Five Histories," and then there were advertisements for typeset editions of the "Twenty-Six Histories." The pre-order price is getting cheaper and cheaper. We have seen the sample pages of the "Twenty-Five Histories," which are printed with photographic zinc plates. There is no need to worry about typos, but the font is a bit too small. It can only be used for reference and is not convenient for reading. What about the "Twenty-Six Histories"? I haven't seen the sample pages yet. But since it is typeset, I think it will be typeset with six-point type. The font is not too small, but, but, after seeing too many typos in "popular editions" such as "A New Account of Tales of the World," I can't help but wonder how many old gentlemen with reading glasses have been hired to carefully proofread this popular edition of the "Twenty-Six Histories"?

Proofreading is by no means a mechanical task. If "official history" and the like were proofread in a "mechanical" way, looking at one character at a time, it would be hard to guarantee that there would not be many jokes! The necessary condition for "popular editions" must also be that they are "readable," right?

I don't know why, but I feel that the "eyes" of the camera are always more reliable than human eyes!

It is Better to Have a Thorny Nose 183

— Longgong Gong

Thanks to Mr. N.V. Gogol for writing the story of the nose and to Mr. Xu Xia for translating this work. Thanks to their respectable work, Mr. Nose has been introduced and we have had the pleasure of getting to know him.

I remember in Zhang Tianyi's "Diary of the Ghost Land," the nose was also regarded as something to be treated with caution. The author, to ridicule the concept of people considering the genitals as filthy and sinful organs, planted an unsanitary crime on the nose, so that the people living in the ghost land, both men and women, wore nose covers. However, this also prevented us from seeing its dignified appearance, leaving us with the regret of not being able to recognize it. I hate this harsh custom.

But how did the Fifth-Rank Civil Official Mr. Nose, who warned his master, the Eighth-Rank Collegiate Assessor Kovalev, treat us? He openly and frankly rode around St. Petersburg in a carriage. To avoid clumsy paraphrasing, I'd better do some copying:

"How should I approach him," Kovalev thought, "Look at everything! The dress uniform, the hat... In short, looking at his whole outfit, he must be a Fifth-Rank Civil Official. Damn it, this is terrible!"

He began to cough next to that gentleman, but the nose did not move at all.

"Respected sir..." Kovalev tried to brace himself, saying, "Respected sir..."

"What do you want?" the nose turned his face and replied.

"I really find it very strange, most respected sir... You should know your own whereabouts... But I suddenly saw you on the street... Where? ... Think for yourself..."

"I'm sorry, I don't understand what you're saying... Please speak more clearly."

"How can I speak more clearly?" Kovalev thought, and then braced himself again, continuing, "Naturally... Also, I am a Major. A Major like me, running around without a nose, isn't that too unsightly?... (The transcriber omits a few words)... Please think for yourself... There's really no way, I really... (At this time, Major Kovalev shrugged his shoulders)... Please forgive me... This matter, according to the laws of duty and honor... But you understand this very well yourself..."

"I don't understand at all," the nose replied, "Please speak more clearly."

"Respected sir," Kovalev said without losing his dignity, "Instead, I don't understand what you mean... Our matter is very clear... If you want me to say it... Then, you are... my nose!"

The nose stared at the Major, frowning slightly.

"You're mistaken, respected sir; I am myself. There can't be any close relationship between us. Because looking at the buttons on your clothes, I know that you work in a different government office." After saying this, the nose ignored him.

To be honest, Gogol was too irresponsible. Even if the nose had other tasks, how could he run around everywhere? Moreover, how could Kovalev confirm that the Fifth-Rank Civil Official was his own nose? Most people are not very able to recognize the shape of their own nose, even if they look in the mirror all day long. This is what we know. It is rare for a nose to suddenly refuse to recognize its master.

According to common sense, people's noses are far inferior to those of dogs. In the book "The Call of the Wild," we see that dogs, relying on their noses, are able to sense the slightest vibrations in the air, thus knowing where there are enemies, where there is food, or whether it will be sunny or rainy tomorrow. But human tasks are much more difficult than dogs: which path is profitable, which behavior can please the master, which clever plan can effortlessly kill people, which maneuver will consolidate one's own power, highlight one's reputation, and exert one's instinct, and what is especially difficult is how to achieve labor-saving but easy success; like a writer, without having to exert the effort of writing, but permanently dominate the literary world... All of this requires a nose that can sniff and drill, a nose that is even more powerful than a dog, to be able to accomplish.

Because of this, people can train their noses, let them out, drill into places that the body can't drill into, and make sounds of "humming," which are both flattering and contemptuous, which is easy to imagine. Moreover, people with more wisdom than Kovalev can decorate it, so that it does not develop stagnation (called acne in Cantonese), just like savages, engraving patterns on it. This is more charming, easier to recognize and manage, and will not be as absurd and rampant as the Fifth-Rank Civil Official.

Everything about our ancestors was more perfect and intelligent than us, and many people are currently proving this, and such a proposal can also be made for the reform of the earliest part of this body.

October 6, 1934.

The Life and Origin of Wheat 184

— Mao Sheng

Wheat is the most important food in the world. Although Chinese people in many places eat rice, they also eat wheat, and wheat is still grown a lot; it is often seen. If you take a few grains of wheat and put them on moist soil, you will see them gradually absorb moisture and swell. After a few days, a tender white root will emerge from one end of the wheat grain. The first roots that emerge are often three, unlike barley, which often has five, or beans, which only have one. The root grows from the lower part of the embryo, at which time the embryo is still inside the wheat grain, lying sideways in a corner at one end of the wheat grain. Soon, the upper end of the embryo also pierces through, and then you see green tender leaves. Next to the embryo there is also a shield-shaped organ, which remains in the wheat grain, and most botanists recognize it as a successive cotyledon, which remains in the wheat grain and is used to absorb the nutrients inside. When the seedling is able to stand on its own, the nutrients inside the wheat grain have also been used up, and the transformed cotyledon withers, and the wheat grain is separated from the seedling.

After the wheat germinates, fine roots gradually grow at the lower part, and green leaves grow at the upper part, and the stem also grows. Its first leaf is shaped like a spearhead, and is incompletely grown, and the second leaf is the same, and then fully developed leaves grow. If there is adequate sunlight, air, and nutrients in the soil are not lacking, it will grow up.

Grown wheat, often seen in the fields, it grows hollow, segmented stalks, with narrow, grass-like leaves growing on the nodes. Subsequently, ears grow on the stalks, and many small flowers grow on the ears. Those small flowers are grown extremely small and simple. Each small flower is wrapped on the outside by two pieces of husk, which are parts equivalent to the sepals of ordinary flowers. Inside there are even smaller two small petals, almost invisible without a magnifying glass. This is probably the part equivalent to the petals, but it has degenerated and become very small. Next are three stamens, with long filaments and pollen-bearing parts, called anthers. In the center is a pistil, with two stigmas on top, split into feathery shapes, which are the parts that receive pollen.

The ear grows, and the flowers also mature, and it unfolds. The flowering time may be early or late depending on the climate, but according to records, it is often at four o'clock in the morning on a sunny day. After an hour or two, it closes again. When it is open, if a breeze blows, carrying the pollen and dropping it on the stigmas of other flowers, the ovules in the ovary are fertilized; flowers that have not been fertilized are fertilized by their own pollen after closing. Most plants must be fertilized before they can bear fruit, like some cottonseeds and bananas, unfertilized fruits will also grow, but they do not contain seeds inside.

Its ovule grows, not only growing into a young embryo, but also producing endosperm that will provide nutrients for its germination in the future. Endosperm is mostly flour, in addition to protein and fat. After the wheat grains turn yellow and ripen, they become the wheat seeds that are planted.

Wheat belongs to the so-called annual type of plant, it withers after flowering and fruiting once in a year. Although many annual plants, wheat is the same, if it is prevented from flowering and fruiting, it can also live for more than a year, but under normal circumstances, it only lives for one year (actually only a few months). However, plants that flower once are not necessarily all annual. Some plants, such as the common chickweed, anciently called fanlu, grow, flower, bear fruit, and die quickly, and can grow several times a year. Many plants, such as radishes or turnips, germinate this year, store nutrients in the swelling formed by the connection of the roots and stems, for flowering and fruiting next year, some bamboos flower and die once after decades, agave, growing in its native land of Mexico, flowers after eight to ten years, growing on the Mediterranean coast, takes twenty to fifty years to flower, and the years of flowering in other places are even longer, hence the name "century plant." But it only flowers once in its life, and its nature is different from plants such as peaches and plums that flower every year and bloom for many years.

The nutrients stored in the wheat grains for the growth of the embryo are the main food of mankind. These nutrients are created by the leaves using carbon dioxide in the air, moisture and minerals in the soil, with the help of sunlight, in parts containing green matter. Wheat-growing areas in the world occupy about 400,000 square miles. Wheat is grown almost everywhere from the Arctic Circle to the highlands of the equator, and yellow wheat grains can be seen throughout the year.

The place of origin of this widely cultivated wheat is still unclear to this day. There are many species and varieties of wheat, and botanists divide them into three categories. The first category has very small grains and low nutritional value, and is now rarely cultivated. This category is called Einklrn. The second category is slightly better, and is called Emmer. The third type can be used to make bread. The first type is found wild in various parts of Asia Minor. The wild type of the second type is found in Syria, probably in southern Syria to the Moab Mountains. Only the widely cultivated type of wheat has never been seen as a wild species. The British agricultural botanist Percival once suggested that its ancestor should be a hybrid of Emmer and another grass species (Aegiops Ovata or Ae. Cylindrica). In recent years, another botanist, Gates, said that wheat should be a hybrid of wild Emmer and wild Emmer. According to various studies, its earliest cultivation site was in southwestern Asia.

In 1926, the Chinese botanist Vavilov published a paper "Research on the Origin of Cultivated Plants," also saying that the earliest cultivation site of wheat should be in southwestern Asia. Vavilov opposed the opinion of the earlier botanist de Conodlle. de Conodlle's famous work "The Origin of Cultivated Plants" was published in 1882, saying that the place of origin of cultivated plants should be near where the wild species of that plant grows. Vavilov said that the earliest place of cultivation can only be determined from where there are the most cultivated varieties. The place with the most cultivated varieties of wheat is first eastern Afghanistan, followed by Persia, and then Transcaucasia. According to Vavilov's opinion, Afghanistan is the earliest place of origin of wheat. Planting in Persia was also early, and Transcaucasia is a "secondary center," which means that it was imported from various places. Other researchers agree that wheat originated in southwestern Asia, but there are slight differences in the details. Sometimes researchers believe that Transcaucasia should be the earliest center of origin of wheat, and Afghanistan does not seem to be the earliest place of origin. Persia may be the earliest cultivation site, but it cannot be determined. The investigation into the earliest place of origin of wheat is a very complex issue, and it is understandable that researchers today cannot agree on opinions, but after another period of investigation in the future, they will naturally tend to be consistent.

Led by Director Jiao and Chief Instructor Ouyang

Instructors from 50 schools including Jiaotong University and Merchant Marine attended

The details are recorded as follows:

▲ Participating Instructors: Including He Suting of Jiaotong University, Tao Yishan of Merchant Marine, Zhao Zhuzhong of Jinan University, Wei Benning and Zeng Dehui of Tongji University, Li Gui of Fudan University, Cheng Wen of Guanghua University, Xia Zhijie of Daxia University, Ma Houwu of the Law School, and 50 others, gathered at the Military Training Association on Daji Road at 8:30 am. First, it is very hard for the instructors to come to Shanghai to take charge of military training in various schools in this abnormal state and complicated situation, so I would like to express my condolences to everyone. Second, I would like to take this opportunity to offer a few suggestions. The academic atmosphere in Shanghai schools has been slightly better in the past two or three years, and the result of military training is also a part of the effect.
