Special Telecommunications Issue

Voices of the Telecommunications Industry

Worship Domestic Products 227

— Lvb冰

The public advocates domestic products, newspapers promote domestic products, domestic product year, domestic product bargains, national salvation and survival depend on domestic products.

To make the society widely purchase domestic goods, on the one hand, a detailed investigation of domestic production should be carried out, and on the other hand, manufacturing should be encouraged. Although domestic products are abundant and raw materials are abundant, the industry is not thriving and there are not many products. Even if you want to use domestic products to suppress foreign goods, the result is still practically impossible. Leaving aside other things, let's talk about telecommunications.

Telecommunications has a history of more than fifty years since its establishment. A glimpse of telecommunications machinery shows that most of them are imported. They come with machines, we go with currency, and the amount of leakage is considerable every year. As for line materials, copper wires and iron wires cannot be made domestically, which is of course not to be mentioned. Our country is known for producing porcelain, but insulators are magnetic materials. They have been repeatedly imitated in Jingdezhen, but due to cost concerns, they have not been fully improved for practical use. The so-called real domestic products are probably only the wooden poles along the line. Only a few remain, which is a pity to say.

People engaged in the telecommunications industry, and those who have interacted with reporters, often hear their opinions, and all have a psychology of worshiping domestic products. However, in the past, the Ministry of Communications rarely advocated machinery manufacturing in a practical way, and also rarely conducted detailed investigations on domestic products that could be applied to telecommunications. Individuals, even if they have talent and wisdom, are always troubled by the lack of testing equipment and the weakness of economic strength. In the end, they can only sigh at the ocean. Therefore, the domestic products used in telecommunications are still very few to this day.

The current Ministry of Communications is vigorously promoting domestic products. It has already issued orders to its subordinates to use domestic products, and now it has issued orders to its subordinates to investigate domestic production. The investigation will collect all kinds of domestic materials suitable for telecommunications, so that nothing is missed. In this way, if domestic goods can be used to compensate for the future of telecommunications, even if the cost increases slightly, it will abandon imports and use domestic products. As for manufacturing, it is especially hoped that it will cooperate with technical experts in the industrial and commercial sectors to put telecommunications materials on the road to self-sufficiency.

People in society, all sectors of industry and commerce, those who have made contributions to domestic telecommunications materials, and those who have studied self-made telecommunications materials, are looking forward to the popularization of domestic products and are welcomed by the telecommunications industry, then it is time to rise up upon hearing the news!

One of the New Constructions for the Convenience of Public Communication: The Establishment of Station Postal and Telegraph Agencies 228

— Opened First

Every time we arrive at various train stations, we see crowds of travelers, men, women, old, and young, in countless numbers. Among these groups of travelers, there must be quite a few who need to send telegrams or letters urgently. However, if we observe train stations across the country, which station has the facilities to conveniently send telegrams or letters? Although there are railway telegraph offices in stations, they do not have a wired connection with the local telegraph bureau. They are specifically established to handle station affairs. In places where telegraph bureaus already exist, they are restricted by the regulations of the telegraph bureau from accepting domestic telegrams from travelers. Therefore, travelers at train stations who have urgent matters and want to send telegrams or letters, except for ordinary letters that can be dropped into mailboxes, have to find the local telegraph or post office, which are mostly far from the station. This is very inconvenient for travelers at train stations! To make up for this shortcoming and for the convenience of travelers at general stations, the transportation authorities recently negotiated a cooperative method with the Railway Department, resulting in the creation of "Station Postal and Telegraph Agencies." Now, I will briefly describe the contents of the station postal and telegraph agencies to the readers:

1. Station postal and telegraph agencies are attached to the most suitable locations within various stations;

2. The affairs of station postal and telegraph agencies are handled by the Railway Bureau on behalf of the telegraph and post offices, with designated personnel from the Railway Bureau handling the work concurrently;

3. The business hours of station postal and telegraph agencies are the same as the usual business hours of the stations where they are located.

4. The duties of station postal and telegraph agencies are defined as follows: (A) Selling stamps, accepting various ordinary, registered, express, and airmail items, and sealing and dispatching outgoing mail packages. (B) Receiving domestic or Hong Kong and Macau telegrams from travelers and the public, and delivering incoming domestic and international telegrams (limited to telegrams delivered to passengers on trains and telegrams received by stations without telegraph bureaus).

5. Postage and quotations are charged according to the regulations of the post and telegraph offices, without any additional fees.

6. Important railway stations are connected to local telegraph bureaus by wires. Where there is a large volume of telegram traffic, Morse key and sounder or teleprinters are used. In other places, telephone sets are installed, and telegrams are transmitted by telephone, or the telegraph bureau is notified to send someone to collect them (limited to particularly lengthy official military telegrams and foreign language telegrams that are prone to errors, or when the Railway Bureau's own telegraph services are particularly busy).

The above is a general description of the internal organization of station postal and telegraph agencies. If all stations have these postal and telegraph agencies, then travelers at the stations can avoid the hassle of running around to find places to send telegrams and letters when they have urgent matters. However, these station postal and telegraph agencies are still in their initial stages. The transportation and railway authorities have decided to first pilot them at the Shanghai North Station, Shanghai South Station, Nanjing Xiaguan, Hangzhou City Station, Suzhou, Wuxi, Zhenjiang, and Jiaxing on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo lines. After achieving significant results, they will be expanded to stations on various lines throughout the country.

In recent years, the transportation authorities have held a very ambitious vision. On the one hand, based on the principle of commercializing state-owned enterprises, they have worked hard to improve and innovate, with all facilities and reforms being based on the premise of benefiting the people and aiming for the widespread development of the industry. On the other hand, with a spirit of cooperation, they first seek close liaison between their own postal, telecommunications, and aviation sectors, and then further liaise with other state-owned enterprises, to integrate the entire transportation industry and increase the efficiency of information dissemination. Therefore, the establishment of such station postal and telegraph agencies through the cooperation of the transportation and railway departments is not only for the convenience of the people, but also has a significant relationship to the transmission of information and the consolidation of national defense in the future. I hope that both parties will work hard to promote this, so that these station postal and telegraph agencies will be widespread throughout the country's stations in the shortest possible time.

Let's look at our eastern neighbor, Japan. Their train stations and post offices have very close communication links, and their telecommunications regulations clearly stipulate that a separate room must be set aside in each train station for communication between the train station and the post office. It can be seen that the work of this kind of communication link is very important. At a time when the country's situation is frequently in danger and foreign troubles are imminent, we should promote its success with the spirit of "cooperation" that President Wang has instructed us in this important communication work.

Remote Control Telephone Cables Used by Broadcasting Radio Stations (1) 229

— Wang Dachun

The rapid advancement of broadcasting in modern countries has increased the need for highly efficient remote control telephone cables in terms of design and manufacturing. The design of this type of telephone cable must be suitable for the spoken language of broadcasting, ensuring accurate pronunciation, and must also achieve clear and pure results when broadcasting various types of music, without reducing or distorting the sound. When radio engineers encounter this type of problem, they can use the existing long-distance telephone cables of the telephone bureau to create a remote control network, connecting one broadcasting station with other broadcasting stations in different locations, so that the music programs of each station can be broadcast to each other; or they can bury dedicated remote control telephone cables, directly connecting the music room with the broadcasting station, so that the programs emitted in the broadcasting music room can be broadcast.

When selecting or designing the core wire of a remote control telephone cable, there are two important properties that must be paid attention to: (1) The core wire must be able to transmit every note in the music, so that there is extremely accurate sound; in other words, it must have a full and wide frequency range (Wide Frequency Range) that is sufficient to match the sound wave frequency on the instrument, so that even the highest notes can be accurately transmitted; (2) The core wire must not be affected by attenuation when transmitting various frequencies, that is, the various transmission frequencies should not change regardless of the amplitude used. Furthermore, this core wire must not be affected by the induction of other nearby lines or strong lines; the result of the induction, whether it is caused by telephone calls, telegraph signals, or strong currents of electricity, can cause the broadcast music program to become unclear or uneven.

Using overhead wires for remote control circuits can also achieve a wide frequency band without discovering attenuation phenomena, because overhead wires have their own characteristics and can transmit high frequencies without attenuation problems. However, the facts tell us that when remote control lines use overhead wires, they are too obviously affected by the outside world. For example, lightning in the atmosphere or strong currents from nearby power lines can cause great damage to this type of non-packaged remote control line. For this reason, the remote control lines used by broadcasting stations must be cables, because their core wires are wrapped in metal (Metallic Shield), which can isolate the induction of the outside world. However, ordinary long-distance telephone cables, which must use Loading Coil to avoid attenuation of the conversation, cannot be used as remote control lines for broadcasting stations because their frequency band is relatively too small and does not have the ability to transmit the sound waves of the broadcast. The frequency in the metal circuit in ordinary two-wire circuit long-distance telephone cables is only 2,700 cycles per second (P.P.S; or Period Per Second), and the frequency in the phantom circuit is slightly higher, but only 3,500 cycles per second. Modern telephone cables have been improved several times due to the need for higher frequencies for communication efficiency, and all frequencies have been improved to 3,400 cycles per second in the metal circuit and 4,300 cycles per second in the phantom circuit. However, at this level, there is still a long way to go to use it as a remote control line to transmit music programs. The latest type of telephone cable used as a remote control line to transmit piano and violin notes should have a frequency of 10,000 cycles per second, and the circuit must be equipped with appropriate load coils for satisfactory results.

On Telegraph Rates 230

— Zhen

The level of telegraph rates is a major issue in the history of a country's transportation. If the price is too high, it is not affordable for the economic capacity of the general public, resulting in very few beneficiaries, which violates the purpose of state-owned enterprises. If the price is too low, it is not acceptable for the value of the work of the enterprise itself, leading to unsustainable operations, which is not the principle of commercial policy. How to make the price appropriate, taking the best and discarding the worst? On the one hand, we should investigate the national economic capacity, and on the other hand, base it on the value of the enterprise itself. There is much room for discussion and research in weighing the gains and losses. European and American countries attach great importance to the issue of telegraph rates and often have organizations of rate committees to conduct research. The formulation of international rates is a focal point of discussion at international telecommunications conferences. This is because the telecommunications industry has a great impact on a country's economy, politics, and culture, and pricing requires careful and thorough consideration.

Commentators often criticize China's telegraph rates as being higher than those of other countries. However, according to surveys and statistics (see the comparison of telegraph rates in various countries and China in the 18th issue of this publication), Germany, Belgium, the United States, and other countries all have higher rates per word for Chinese telegrams than China. In terms of the lowest price per telegram, almost all countries except Japan have higher rates than China. If we consider the ratio of area to price, China has the largest area and the cheapest fees. Therefore, the claim that China's rates are too high is not a sound argument.

Commentators also say that the current domestic rates are not affordable for the economic capacity of the general public. This statement is reasonable, but according to the history of domestic rates, it is not accurate. The following is a list of domestic telegraph rates over the years:

Comparison of Domestic Telegraph Rates Over the Years

Chinese Language Plain Language Chinese Cipher or Foreign Language Effective Date Remarks

Within Province Between Provinces Within Province Between Provinces

10 cents Add 2 cents per province 20 cents Add 4 cents per province From August of the 20th year of the Guangxu reign

10 cents Add 3 cents per province 20 cents Add 6 cents per province From January of the 23rd year of the Guangxu reign

8 cents Add 2.4 cents per province 16 cents Add 4.8 cents per province From January of the 1st year of the Xuantong reign The above were set by the Postal and Communications Department of the Qing Dynasty

6 cents 12 cents 9 cents 18 cents From the 1st year of the Republic of China

8 cents 15 cents 16 cents 30 cents From November of the 11th year of the Republic of China

6 cents 12 cents 9 cents 18 cents From January of the 12th year of the Republic of China

7 cents 14 cents 11 cents 22 cents From February of the 16th year of the Republic of China The above were set by the Ministry of Communications of the Beijing government

8 cents 16 cents 16 cents 32 cents From September of the 16th year of the Republic of China

10 cents 10 cents 20 cents 20 cents From October 10 of the 17th year of the Republic of China The above were set by the Ministry of Communications of the National Government

Looking at the table on the right, from August of the 20th year of the Guangxu reign to the 3rd year of the Xuantong reign, a progressive system of adding fees based on the number of provinces was adopted, with the highest rate being 40 cents per word. From the 1st year of the Republic of China to October 9 of the 17th year, a system of rates within and between provinces was adopted, with the highest rate being 8 cents within the province and 16 cents between provinces. From October 10 of the 17th year, a unified system was adopted, with a flat rate of 10 cents regardless of whether it was within or between provinces. This rate was already cheaper than the rates of previous years. Since January of the 22nd year, the names and addresses of recipients of domestic Chinese telegrams within 15 characters have been calculated as 5 characters uniformly, and express telegrams have been reduced to twice the normal rate. This method is the cheapest compared to the rates of any previous era, and the current standards for material costs, the value of purchasing equipment, and the needs of employee salaries are not as high as in any previous era. The people of the past 50 years have been able to afford the higher rates of previous years, which has already been proven by facts. Therefore, according to the rates of previous years, the claim that the current rates are too high is not a factual statement.

According to statistics from the Ministry of Communications, since the implementation of the unified rate in the 17th year, the annual operating loss has been approximately 1.1 million yuan. Since the revision of the method for calculating recipient names and addresses this year, the annual loss is approximately 480,000 yuan. Under such a large amount of sacrifice and in the extremely difficult economic situation of the telecommunications administration, some people at the telecommunications administration conference last month, in view of the repeated price increases of the postal service and railways in recent years, advocated restoring the system of rates within and between provinces to provide relief. However, the general assembly decided that the rate issue should be addressed by streamlining operations and facilitating the public, and that the current rates should be maintained. The intention is that if there are possibilities for reducing expenses in the telecommunications administration and there are hopes for expanding telecommunications services, they should be done as much as possible, and that they are unwilling to change the current telegraph rates and increase the burden on the public. This spirit of working hard to improve and facilitate the public is truly commendable!

Commentary on the Case of the Yongli and Yongzeng Joint Silver Firms in Tianjin Illegally Establishing Radio Stations 231

— Di You

(The process of solving the case) Initially, the authorities of the Ministry of Communications received a secret report that the Yongli and Yongzeng joint silver firms in Tianjin had illegally established a radio station on the building at 51 Yaohua Lane in the British Concession to communicate with Shanghai. The ministry immediately secretly instructed the Tianjin Telegraph Bureau, the Radio Station, and the affiliated organizations of the Telephone Bureau to cooperate closely in the investigation. The investigation concluded that the location of the two silver firms' illegally established radio station was indeed at the aforementioned location. They then, together with the Public Security Bureau of the provincial capital, consulted the British Municipal Council and obtained a search warrant to conduct a search. When they first entered, they saw nothing except two telephones. After a thorough search, they found a receiver, charger, codebook, telegraph drafts, and other parts in the dressing table. They also arrested a telegraph operator and a partner of the two silver firms on the spot. They also carefully checked the electrical wiring in the entire room, which was connected to the ceiling. When they sawed open the ceiling, they found a transmitter, two transformers, a wave meter, and a telegraph key. The British Municipal Council then extradited all the stolen goods and criminals to the Public Security Bureau for trial in court.

(Subsequent disposal) After the event, the Ministry of Communications recognized that various parties had assisted greatly in solving the case of the two silver firms illegally establishing a radio station. In order to reward the meritorious and facilitate future work, the ministry specially awarded a first-class medal each to the directors of the Telegraph and Telephone Bureaus, the chief engineer of the Radio Station, the director of the Public Security Bureau, and the director of the Police Department of the British Municipal Council. The hard-working telegraph personnel from the two bureaus and stations were each given bonuses. In addition, a large sum of money was allocated to the Tianjin Public Security Bureau and the Police Department to be distributed to the police officers. The criminal part of the case has been formally prosecuted by the Tianjin Local Court Prosecutor's Office for theft, and the part of the case involving infringement of telegraph business has been carefully calculated by the Telegraph Bureau and attached to the private prosecution. The main criminal in the case, the manager of the Yongli and Yongzeng joint silver firms, fled in fear of punishment after the incident and has disappeared without a trace. An order has been issued to strictly arrest him and bring him to justice. Furthermore, since the two silver firms used the city telephone system to transmit telegrams between the two silver firms and the illegally established radio station, the Tianjin Telephone Bureau has been ordered to remove all the telephones installed by the two silver firms as a warning to those who use state-owned telephones for illegal communication. Furthermore, the authorities of the Ministry of Communications believe that illegally established radio stations have been discovered in Tianjin in recent years, which has greatly affected the future of telecommunications administration. In order to thoroughly eliminate them, advertisements have been placed in major newspapers in Tianjin, offering rewards for reporting illegal radio stations.

(Conclusion) Article 3 of the Telecommunications Regulations states: "The following telecommunications (omitted) may be established by local governments, public or private organizations, or individuals after approval by the Executive Yuan of the National Government, the Ministry of Communications, or other authorized agencies." Therefore, it is not permitted by the Telecommunications Regulations to establish a radio station privately without the approval of the competent authority. Furthermore, this case involves as many as eight criminals, and the illegal radio station has engaged in eavesdropping on news telegrams from various places and soliciting commercial telegrams for profit. Considering the circumstances, it is different from other cases of illegally established telecommunications. The transmission of radio waves relies on radio waves, so those who illegally establish radio stations can listen to the radio waves and telegrams emitted by public radio stations in addition to private communication. Considering that electricity should be considered a thing under Article 340, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law, there is no doubt that it constitutes the crime of organized theft under the Criminal Law. Therefore, the Tianjin Prosecutor's Office's public prosecution for theft is a strict and just measure. Furthermore, in recent years, the trend of illegally establishing radio stations for secret communication has been rampant, and the harm it causes is great. The greater harm is that it affects local public order, and the lesser harm is that it disrupts the financial market, and the harm to state-owned telecommunications is particularly significant. However, although this type of illegally established radio station has been repeatedly cracked down on by the Ministry of Communications, criminals value profits over the law and still dare to try it, stubbornly unaware of the warning. The reasons for this are that wireless radio talent, equipment, and materials are easy to obtain, and the punishment regulations are not strict enough to warn the criminals. Therefore, the fundamental solution is that the Ministry of Communications should find ways to unify and manage wireless radio talent, materials, and equipment, so that those who illegally establish radio stations lose their dependence. On the other hand, the Ministry of Communications should submit a request to the Executive Yuan to consult the Legislative Yuan to add a special article to the draft revision of the Criminal Law, imposing severe penalties on those who illegally establish radio stations, illegally communicate, and use them. The so-called "ruling a chaotic country requires severe punishments" is probably the same. Perhaps the villains will know to restrain themselves. It is heard that the Ministry of Communications is planning to increase the penalties for the latter, and for the sake of maintaining our country's wireless telecommunications industry, which is just beginning, it is necessary to realize it as soon as possible!

"Those Who Speak Should Have Their Own Electricity" 232

— Guo Song

丨丨The Result of Resolving the Public Telephone Problem丨丨

In the 19th issue of this publication, Mr. Lü Bing raised the issue of public telephones for public discussion, and inferred that the reason why public telephones have not been promoted in our country is because (A) the problem of use and (B) the problem of installation have not been properly resolved, so it is appropriate to establish the principle of both facilitating the public and considering business. It has been found that public telephones have been installed in various prosperous cities in our country, either operated by the Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications or managed by merchants. However, because there are no guidelines, the business regulations and management methods established in various places are inconsistent and mostly inappropriate. It is not enough to arouse the public's interest in sending telegrams? The lack of development of public telephones is the main reason. Now, the Ministry of Communications has formulated one type of "General Rules for the Operation of Public Telephones by the Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications" and one type of "General Rules for the Ministry of Communications to Recruit Merchants to Manage Public Telephones", which have been announced and implemented on September 22 of this year. The former is to solve the problem of use, and the latter is to solve the problem of installation. With these fixed general rules to comply with, the problem of public telephones has been resolved.

It has been found that the installation of public telephones is more important than that of private telephones. Why? Private telephones only provide calls for individuals or a store or an organization, and the scope is very small; public telephones provide calls for all citizens, and the need is greater. Moreover, at a time when the telephone business in our country is not yet developed, it is necessary to promote the business so that the public is happy to use it and develop the habit of calling, and then the business can be developed.

The purpose of the two general rules announced by the Ministry of Communications is entirely for the convenience of the public. Although its initial implementation has indeed been affected by the problems of (A) use and (B) installation mentioned by Mr. Lü Bing, it does not harm the business. It is not without loss, but in line with the principle of commercializing state-owned enterprises and making them more public, public telephones will never be ignored due to temporary minor losses. Moreover, once public telephones are developed, the public will feel the convenience and need for sending telegrams, which in turn can promote the popularity of private telephones?

When we are wandering around the streets and have something important to tell someone or an organization, we often suffer from the inability to communicate, or we are often rejected when we go to various businesses to borrow telephones (which is actually reasonable), resulting in a feeling of being unable to move forward or backward and having no one to tell. Now that the general rules for public telephones have been announced, we will see the installation of public telephones in prosperous areas of the city. Each time, you only need to pay a toll fee of 3 to 5 cents of silver to enjoy the convenience of calling. Mr. Sun Yat-sen's farmer policy said, "Those who till the land should have their own land." After the public telephone problem of the Ministry of Communications is resolved, isn't it "those who speak should have their own electricity"?

Several Small Hurdles to Sending Telegrams (Continued) 233

— Qinghua

In the previous two issues, twelve ways to save money have already been discussed. Now, let's talk about how to make telegrams fast and accurate:

(1) Urgent Telegrams: Urgent telegrams are like special appointments at a hospital outpatient clinic. The telegraph office sends such telegrams immediately upon receipt, which is much faster than ordinary telegrams. Although the fee is doubled, people don't care about a dollar or two when there are extremely urgent matters, as long as the telegram arrives quickly. Therefore, merchants mostly send urgent telegrams for market information so that it arrives instantly and they can make various important transactions. Ordinary private individuals may also send urgent telegrams if there are the most urgent matters so that the recipient can receive it immediately.

(2) Using the Telephone to Transmit Telegrams: The most time-consuming and laborious part of sending a telegram is that the sender must send the telegram to the telegraph office by messenger or in person. This process takes at least five minutes, and sometimes dozens of minutes. After the telegraph office receives the telegram, the time it takes to transmit it from station A to station B, or then to station C, is relatively short. However, when station B or C dispatches a messenger for delivery after receiving the telegram, it takes a considerable amount of time again. Therefore, if senders and receivers want to speed up the telegram and save the time of dispatching messengers, it is best to use a local telephone to transmit the telegram to the telegraph office over the phone, which is the most convenient. When sending a telegram, just inform the telegraph office of the text over the phone, and the telegraph office will send it immediately. When receiving a telegram, the telegraph office transmits the text to the recipient. In this way, both parties save the procedure and time of dispatching messengers, and each telegram can be faster by at least ten or twenty minutes, or even one or two hours. This is such an important hurdle!

(3) Installing Dedicated Line Telegraph and Telephone Machines: Merchants with a large volume of telegram traffic often use local telephones to transmit telegrams. However, because the telegraph office or their own telephone is occupied, delays are inevitable. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications has come up with a good solution, which is to allow merchants to apply to the telegraph office to install dedicated lines and rent telegraph machines, or to rent dedicated telephone lines and telephones from the local telephone bureau, so that they can transmit telegrams to the telegraph office via dedicated lines without any delay. Detailed procedures can be obtained from the telegraph office or our newspaper.

(4) Forwarding Telegrams: If the sender is unsure of the recipient's location, such as when traveling to various places on official business or for leisure, it is difficult to determine where the recipient is when sending the telegram. In this case, the sender can write two or more place names and addresses. The telegraph office first sends it to the first place name. If it is found that the recipient has left that place, it is then sent to the second place name. If the recipient has left, it is then sent to the third place name, and so on, until it is delivered. This is a very convenient method. As for the fee, the sender can pay the fee for the first leg in advance, and the remaining fees can be collected from the recipient. The sender can also pay all the fees if they wish. If the sender wants to know when this type of forwarding telegram has been delivered, they can use the "inform upon delivery" method. Add the words "inform upon delivery" to the beginning of the telegram (counted as one word for billing), and pay an additional fee equivalent to six words of an ordinary telegram. The telegraph office will then send a notification to the sender when the telegram has been delivered, informing the sender that the telegram was delivered on a certain day at a certain time. When the sender receives this telegram, they know that the telegram has been delivered and can rest assured! I'm afraid very few people understand this hurdle of sending telegrams. I hope readers will tell their relatives and friends, so that when they encounter this situation, they can calmly send a forwarding telegram, without having to send one telegram to place A first, and then send another telegram to place B after the telegraph office informs them that it could not be delivered. This not only avoids delaying a lot of time, but also saves a lot of trouble. It is indeed a very convenient way to send telegrams!

(5) Transferring Telegrams: If the recipient sometimes has to go elsewhere due to important matters, but anticipates that a telegram will be sent to a certain place, in order to avoid delaying the telegram, they can go in person or notify the telegraph office by letter that if a telegram addressed to them is received, it should be immediately transferred to the telegraph office at the place they are going to and delivered to the recipient. The fee can be paid in advance by the recipient, or paid upon receipt. Also, if the recipient did not contact the telegraph office before leaving, their family members or relatives can also request that the telegram be transferred to a certain place, but the fee must be paid by the requester. This method seems similar to sending another telegram, but if the recipient notifies the telegraph office in advance, the telegram does not need to be delivered by messenger, but can be directly transferred to a certain place, which is much faster! Furthermore, if you ask family members or relatives to resend a telegram from a certain place, then at least you must add words such as "telegram from a certain place" to the text, which will cost more!

(6) Self-Translation of Code: I have already mentioned self-translation of code when discussing ways to save money. However, there is another advantage to translating code yourself, which is that the telegraph office can send the telegram immediately upon receipt without delay. If the telegraph office is asked to translate it, because there are more than one or two telegrams to be translated, busy telegraph offices often have several or even dozens of telegrams to be translated at the same time. In that case, even if the telegraph office dispatches three or four people to translate them, there will inevitably be some delay, which will certainly be slower than self-translated telegrams. Therefore, self-translation of code is also a small hurdle to making telegrams fast!

The above mentioned six hurdles are all ways to make telegrams fast. Now let's talk about how to make telegrams accurate:

(1) Writing Clearly: People sending telegrams often write the telegram text sloppily because the matter is urgent. When telegraph office personnel receive it, they may misread it and send it incorrectly, causing the recipient to misunderstand the meaning of the telegram and think it is the telegraph office's negligence. In foreign language telegrams, A and O, E and L, B and F, Q and G, etc. are very similar. If the writing is blurry, it is easy to misread and send incorrectly. Also, in telegrams typed by a typewriter, sometimes the typist is lazy and does not erase the misspelled letters, but instead types another letter on top of the letter, so it will become a letter that looks like both A and O, making it impossible for telegraph office personnel to identify it. This is the fault of the sender themselves. If it is wrong, they have to bear the responsibility! Therefore, writing telegrams clearly is a small hurdle to making telegrams accurate. Furthermore, the sender's name and address must be clearly stated at the bottom of the telegram so that the telegraph office can inquire or notify the sender if there is an error in the telegram or if it cannot be delivered; otherwise, it will be impossible to notify them, delaying their telegram.

(2) Proofreading Telegrams: If there are numbers of silver or money, or important words and phrases in the telegram, which are of great importance and cannot be wrong, then the sender can request the telegraph office to proofread the telegram during transmission in order to ensure accuracy and reliability. This type of telegram is called a proofread telegram. Write the word "proofread" at the beginning of the telegram, and pay an additional proofreading fee, calculated at one-half of the ordinary telegram fee. The text can be guaranteed to be error-free. If, unfortunately, an error occurs again, the telegraph office can refund the entire fee, but this is very rare. Although senders have to pay an additional half fee for this method, the text can be absolutely guaranteed to be accurate, so that it does not delay important matters, which is also worthwhile!

(3) Write the Original Text When Self-Translating Code: As mentioned above, self-translating code can save money and speed things up. However, it is inevitable to mistranslate code in a hurry. Therefore, it is best to write the original text on the bottom of the telegram so that telegraph office personnel can check the code against the original text when receiving it, and correct any errors. This can also be considered a small hurdle to making telegrams accurate!

I have mentioned so many hurdles for sending telegrams above, but it is inevitable that some things are missing. It is best for readers to write to our newspaper for a copy of the "Abstract of New Regulations on Saving Telegraph Fees" and other telegraph regulations (see the advertisement in the upper right corner), and read them carefully. Then you will understand all kinds of hurdles without any omissions!

Bi-Weekly News 234

— A Contributor

Improved Method for Translating and Sending Chinese Telegrams: In the past, the Ministry of Communications established a method for free translation of incoming telegrams for the convenience of the public, which has been well received by the public since its implementation. However, the incoming telegrams mixed handwritten code with translated text, making it inconvenient and not very neat for recipients to read. Therefore, a few months ago, the Ministry of Communications specially purchased a Chinese typewriter and sent it to the Nanjing Telegraph Bureau for trial. All incoming Chinese code telegrams only type the text and do not copy the code. Each line can type more than ten characters, which is very convenient for recipients to read, and the typeface is clear and the image is excellent. In order to promote this, the Ministry of Communications has specially ordered all subordinate stations to translate and transcribe the text of all incoming Chinese code telegrams received by the Weston machine, and not to copy the code. The major bureaus and stations will also purchase Chinese typewriters for application according to the example of the Nanjing Bureau.

Method for Counting Words in English News Telegrams: English news telegrams often contain abbreviations and irregular compound words. Because telegraph offices are required to count them as two or three words according to regulations, this often causes misunderstandings for senders. The Ministry of Communications has now established a method for counting words: all non-commonly seen abbreviations and compound words not listed in English dictionaries should be charged according to the number of words that should be counted when writing them out in full. A small booklet has been printed with detailed examples for news reporters to request and avoid misunderstandings. (This booklet can also be requested from our newspaper by letter)

Supplement to the Shen Bao Local Edition

Talking Points

Child Welfare Issues 235

— Qiong Sheng

The conference of child welfare leaders, bringing together experts in child education, hygiene, psychology, and other fields, has already "jointly explored" the issues, successfully completed its work, and announced its closure. It is reported that the resolutions reached include the following: (1) Requesting the government to guarantee child welfare undertakings and support their development; (2) Requesting the government to issue arrest warrants for trafficking in women and children, and to reiterate the strict enforcement of the ban on keeping slaves and raising maids; (3) Requesting an order to prohibit underage children from pulling rickshaws; and (4) Requesting the government to formulate a child law as soon as possible.

Chinese children have already fallen into a pitiful state along with the decline of the entire nation. Many poor orphans who have lost their parents in childhood either become beggars, thieves, and die, or countless non-orphaned children also face the same fate due to poverty "since birth." They either become slaves and maids, doing arduous work to make a living, or the sins of selling sons and daughters occur by the thousands under this fundamental cause. Especially in recent years of disasters, poor farmers first kill their children and then commit suicide, exchange children for food, and lead young girls into cities to become "child prostitutes," all of which illustrate the crux of the Chinese child problem.

Now, so many child welfare leaders who hold infants in their arms have gathered at sea to try to save them. Their mentality of "loving my children and extending that love to the children of others" is truly admirable, and I hope that their efforts will "cultivate virtue in their children." However, the trafficking of children and making them do arduous work such as pulling rickshaws certainly makes people "fear and feel compassion," but when they have no way to make a living, they have no choice but to sell their bodies, working like animals to maintain their lives. To seek a paper ban to eliminate this is no different from ordering them to sit and wait for death? Establishing child laws, organizing nurseries, orphanages, baby care centers, child education societies, happiness societies, and health clubs, while compassionate, still, we especially hope to see efforts to eliminate the social roots that trap children in a miserable fate. Otherwise, without addressing the root cause, I have not seen any success.

As this "Children's Year" is about to arrive, we would like to offer this advice to child welfare leaders, and at the same time, we hope that people will be alerted to the fact that in this syphilitic society, the facts of the problem facing children are becoming even more exposed!

South Lake Water Chestnuts 236

— Linlin

When we changed into flannel suits, we were invited by a friend to Jiaxing, the city of Misty Rain Tower. There were four of us going together, all living in the urban circle. We felt an unusual excitement for this short trip, preparing for several days as if attending a serious banquet, and also spending considerable time hesitating about the trip.

Under the high sky, the morning breeze fluttered our colored ties, and we arrived in Jiaxing after a two-hour journey. A friend was already waiting for us on the platform, along with his younger sister. On the way to his home, the six of us were filled with an unusual joy.

Changing the environment, in the eyes of strangers, every tree and blade of grass is a rare flower and plant. We did not stop walking all afternoon, really wanting to find unexpected satisfaction in this new environment. But we did not go to Misty Rain Tower, leaving this scenic spot to enjoy tomorrow. The sun had not yet set. After dinner, we sat by the river behind his house, arguing that we should not waste this lovely autumn night. My friend's younger sister suggested hiring a small boat to cruise the river. Just then, the clear sound of selling water chestnuts came from the river. We knew that Jiaxing's South Lake water chestnuts were so famous, and several of us rushed down the stone steps. The water chestnut seller was a girl, rowing the scull alone, which was very enticing. We bought a basin of water chestnuts and sat on the stone steps to peel them. Perhaps our foreign accents aroused the girl's interest, she forgot her profession. Although she kept shouting "selling water chestnuts," she did not row her scull. My friend's younger sister jokingly asked to rent her boat, which she unexpectedly agreed to. She even rented another small boat for us, and the six of us swarmed onto it like bees.

This was the beginning of the joke. Me, my friend's younger sister, and Qi, who came with us, jumped onto the rented boat. Except for Qi, who could row a few strokes, the two of us could not be sailors, so our boat was always far behind theirs. The water chestnut seller scoffed at us, "If you want to eat water chestnuts, hurry up and catch up." Later, after a while, we caught up, but my friend pulled Qi over, and their boat flew like an arrow, sending waves of laughter from afar.

Helpless, I took up the scull and tried hard to row, but still spinning in circles. So the two of us worked together to row, sweating all over, but the boat did not move forward a few feet, and the boat in front had disappeared. At this time, a boat came towards us. They said that it was now low tide, and it was not easy to row upstream. The two of us had no choice but to drop the scull and let it slowly drift back. In the moonlight, we chatted idly. I don't remember what we talked about now. The boat drifted back to her home by the river, and we sat on the stone steps for a long time before their boat returned.

The next day, we took the night train back to Shanghai. The brother and sister sent us to the station with warm feelings, asking when we would come to Jiaxing again to play for a few more days. Qi replied, "Next year when the water chestnuts are on the market, that girl has made an appointment with me." We parted with laughter.

The following spring, a friend wrote a letter saying that his younger sister was coming to Shanghai to study. But in the autumn, I suddenly received a letter from her saying that her mother did not allow her to come to Shanghai to study, and asked if I could come to Jiaxing to eat South Lake water chestnuts?

It was time to change into flannel suits again. Counting the years, it had been three years. The letter I sent had also been returned by the post office. I really missed the girl's clear sound of selling water chestnuts!

Emotion Tax 237

— Wen Bing

Reading the 50th issue of "Lun Yu", I found the following in "Bi-Weekly News":

Sichuan has recently added a surtax on grain taxes, called "Emotion Tax". It is said that adding this surtax is for the purpose of providing supplies for the stationed troops. In this way, the military and the people will have harmonious feelings, and there will be no drawbacks of extortion from the people.

After reading it, I couldn't help but laugh bitterly and loudly for half an hour, and repeatedly shouted "Oh! Grand!" more than ten times. Still not feeling completely relieved, my fingers started to itch, so I spread out the manuscript paper and tried to elaborate on the three words "Emotion Tax".

Needless to say, this is not only a brand new invention in Sichuan's tax policy, but also the ultimate in tax policy progress. I think this method must neither be "existing since ancient times" nor "imported from foreign countries", but a new initiative of the local authorities. We know very well that Sichuan is quite strange as Sichuan. Take the collection of grain taxes, for example. According to reports in newspapers many times, some have been collected for more than fifty years, some for more than sixty years, and even some for more than eighty years. Then, I think the general statistics are all pre-collected for more than forty years. There won't be a fool who only observes the progress of others and "sticks to the old ways" by only pre-collecting for a few or dozens of years.

In recent years, I have often seen reports in newspapers that Sichuan's politics have been relatively improved, but unexpectedly the sign of its improvement is the establishment of the clever name of "Emotion Tax".

This cannot but be regarded as the cleverness of the local authorities, or perhaps because the surtax on grain taxes is so numerous that it is impossible to add more, and all the names have been exhausted. I racked my brains and wondered whose divine spirit came up with such a method - an unprecedented, unparalleled method.

However, the three words "Emotion Tax" are still a bit harsh and heartbreaking! If it is really as stated in the "Lun Yu": "In this way, the military and the people will have harmonious feelings, and there will be no drawbacks of extortion from the people." Then I will also express my congratulations on behalf of the Sichuan people.

Lemon Milk and Women 238

— Xin

A young couple walked leisurely and lightly. Occasionally passing by fruit stores, the woman would often say: Buy a lemon to take back! Or walking to the entrance of a department store, stopping and saying: Buy a can of milk! The man would always inadvertently chime in: Then buy two more. Do you like to eat this stuff? The woman would smile and not answer. In the end, she always only bought one and a small can. The man would get impatient and hurriedly add: Why buy such a small can? It won't last two days. Just buy two big cans! Milk and lemons are both good things, eating more is okay. But the woman always bought according to her own ideas, not listening to the man's good intentions. The man was really a bit puzzled, why always only buy a small can and a pair?

When getting up together in the morning, the man didn't really pay much attention to the woman's washing up. But the woman would look for a small knife to open the milk early in the morning. The man thought she was hungry, quickly opened it, ready to pour it out and brew, and also brew some coffee to add to it. But the woman snatched it away, took the milk, towel, toothbrush, and other items, and went into the bathroom. When cutting a lemon, the man wanted to help her brew it, but she also didn't need any help. This was strange! Women's temperaments are so strange! Hard to grasp. Taking it into the bathroom, to eat it all alone? That's probably not it. Always loving this set, so he had to see what the reason was. Women are so funny, sneaking into the bathroom to take a look.

Water and towel were all prepared, reaching out a slender and tender ginger shoot-like hand, pouring a little milk into her palm, mixing in some water drops, rubbing her hands together, and wiping it on her face, just like wiping snow cream. The man suddenly laughed: Why are you doing this? Turning her head, she shyly smiled back: Silly, you don't understand… don't mind, go away! The man still hadn't woken up: What does it mean exactly, tell me clearly! Hee hee hee, the woman laughed non-stop, lightly wiping her face: Clumsy, go away, I'll tell you later… The man was full of curiosity, waiting beside her, watching intently.

The woman finished washing up, tidying up for almost half an hour. The man kept teasing her, because his legs were getting sore. With a face full of smiles, she pulled the man into the bedroom, that face like a freshly picked apple, gently touching the man's cheek and face, lightly rubbing her skin against the man's skin: How is it? More delicate, right? More smooth? The man was like he had discovered a strange thing, and laughed in amazement: It is more delicate and smooth! It turned out that women often use milk and lemon juice to wipe their faces, treating it as one of the cosmetic decorations. Washing with this stuff, is indeed "more delicate and smooth!" Not bad at all, lemon milk and women, these days, there are so many interesting things!

Autumn 239

Evening of a Memorial Day 240

— Yi

Two years ago in the autumn, Ade was still a young and strong youth. He and his comrades were transferred to this prosperous metropolis for the first time. At that time, he was so happy in his heart! He had been a soldier for several years, and every year he was only desperately fighting with his brothers. Finally, he got this opportunity to come to this peaceful, happy, and peaceful city to rest. For him, he had never dreamed of such a day for years. But in less than a few months, an unexpected event happened, breaking his dream. What was presented before his eyes was no longer that peaceful, happy, and peaceful city, but a battlefield with artillery fire everywhere. All day long, what flew over his head was only that terrible cannonball and airplane.

The red flag of the sun was planted all over Ade's previous position. After several months of desperate fighting, Ade was lucky enough not to be killed in battle, but he had already become a disabled person. From this time on, in this city, there were always the footprints of this wanderer.

Hunger and cold, day by day, increasingly pressed down on Ade. Even that bowl of coarse rice soldier's meal and that thin cotton coat could not be obtained. Therefore, whenever he suffered too much from the ravages of hunger and cold, he would go crazy and bark like a dog:

"Am I not human? Am I doomed to starve and freeze?"

One autumn passed and then another autumn. Ade wandered through the streets of this city all day long, and lay under the shop awnings on North Sichuan Road all night. When it rained, he couldn't even lie down and walked on the road all night.

Heaven finally showed great compassion to the poor, and stopped the rain a few days ago, and the sun shone brightly all day long. Of course, this was like finding a way out for Ade, but at night, he still cursed heaven.

Today, when the street cleaner was sweeping the road, Ade walked from that small alley onto the road, because today is a memorial day, and there will definitely be more pedestrians on the road. This means that Ade can beg for a little more money to eat a full meal. He knew that he was Chinese, and he should also be happy on this memorial day.

The sun seemed particularly hot today, and the crowded pedestrians on the road were all sweating. No one bothered to take out the coins from their pockets to give to these uninteresting beggars. From morning until afternoon, Ade did not beg for a single coin.

On this memorial day evening, Ade, this disabled man who had been wandering in this city for two years, entered prison for the twenty-third time.

Illness 241

— Jia

Illness, for me, is truly a great threat. In every aspect, it is enough to devastate me and shake my inherent beliefs. After suffering through illness once, my thoughts on life are painted with a deeper layer of grey doubt. If I were not so lacking in material resources, there would not be such a great change. But when I am in dire straits, so poor that I cannot even secure my daily three meals, and then I fall ill, it is not just my thoughts that are shaken, but my entire world that crumbles. At this moment, I will despairingly shout to myself: Let it end like this, let my sorrowful life end quickly. My life is like a ripple on the water's surface in the darkness, appearing and disappearing, without a moon, without stars, and without even a sliver of light to brighten my eyes and lift my spirits! Instead, it is filled with boundless dark clouds and a thick fog of boundless gloom. What hope can I hold onto? I truly no longer wish to live out my days bearing this heavy burden of suffering.

Every day, I wish I could stop breathing sooner rather than later, quietly return to the earthen mound covered with weeds, and sleep forever. That would be my greatest satisfaction. But what method can I use to achieve this goal! Severing my own neck with my own hands would be the most decisive thing to do. But alas, I cannot muster that kind of courage. So, I can only hope that illness will fulfill my wish for me. Therefore, whenever an illness descends upon me, not only do I not feel the slightest terror or fear, but I even feel a sense of joy, as if my hope has been revealed. I secretly rejoice: My long-cherished wish is about to be fulfilled. I fervently pray that my condition will worsen day by day, until it can no longer worsen.

Each time I am bedridden, I hope that the illness will destroy my life. But no, the ending only brings me more and greater suffering. When I am ill, even if I do not take medicine, the illness does not intensify! After a few days, I recover, much to my dismay. It does not get rid of me cleanly and quickly, but it becomes an overly familiar companion, visiting me from time to time. And with each bout of illness, my body naturally becomes weaker and thinner day by day after recovery, and at the same time, my thoughts become increasingly dark and gloomy. In the end, not only do I completely lose hope in everything, but I also become a mere shell, a soulless ghost. Therefore, not only do I curse everything and hate everything, but I especially hate the illness. I originally had a strong affection for it, but now it is using this cruel method to slowly manipulate me and fool me. How can I endure this dry and tasteless life, devoid of all hope?

Insomnia 242

— Luo Shan

It's been ten days since I started counting my insomnia.

My eyes gaze at the clock on the desk; the long hand is on six again, and the short hand is pointing exactly at two o'clock after midnight.

I recite numbers, from one to ten, my eyelids closing and opening, opening and closing. Lying on her side, my companion sleeps soundly, her face pale with melancholy and suffering, breathing outside the covers, that breath resembling the sighs of a dying person.

Suddenly, a threat of death dominates her entire life. And in that moment of thinking about death, all luck and happiness are destroyed under the threat of death. Tilting her head back, she scrutinizes her bluish-grey face once more.

"Two miserable people together..." she murmurs.

"Why can't I sleep?"

She asks herself again, her heart ringing inside like an ancient bell.

Is it almost a nervous breakdown? She worries, and then visions of passing by the gate of the mental hospital during the day appear before her eyes.

How much she detests this death-like life! No sound, moans, medicine bottles, sorrowful faces, her own neurasthenia, insomnia, no appetite... Detestable! A lonely person with a lonely heart, living in this lonely place.

(The day of the end of life is not far away, alas!)

She looks at the short hand again and sighs.

The reason for not being able to sleep is simple: the busy routine during the day, the instability, of course, makes it impossible to sleep soundly at night, unless one is a soulless husk. She feels sad!

A sorrowful heart, a person with a sorrow that no one understands, she can't get a bit of comfort for herself, and she still has to deal with adults and children, forcing herself to smile, spreading the layer of silent air to the most lively atmosphere. She hides her true self, concealing her heartfelt sorrow, daring not to shed a tear or vent her frustration, every day putting on the old routine of a clown on stage, laughing, telling stories, singing lively jazz, everyone enduring the gloomy rainy days of autumn in happiness, but what does she get? She is so uneasy.

(I am in great pain, but I must take care of these things, alas!)

Softly, as if in a dream, dragging her slippers, she extinguishes the lamp, her eyes still shining brightly in the darkness of the night.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

Some Adorable Tidbits About Shirley Temple 246

— Jing Yang

This adorable "little baby," Shirley Temple, is currently filming "Now and Forever" at the Paramount studio. One day, just after Shirley finished filming a scene, the director, Mr. Henry Hathaway, suddenly rushed off. People were puzzled, thinking he had gone mad. Little did they know, he had gone to buy ice cream for Shirley, because her crying scene was so genuine that Hathaway couldn't help but be moved. There was also a star, Gary Cooper, who worked with her on the same set. He was originally an artist who had worked as an illustrator for a newspaper. He used all sorts of methods to get Shirley to sit still for a portrait. After it was finished, he gave her a velvet teddy bear named Grong Bay.

Many people think that Shirley Temple's rise to stardom (she is indeed a star, earning $1,250 per week) was a matter of luck and chance. Of course, whether it's Shirley Temple or Katharine Hepburn, without the help of luck, they wouldn't be able to reach stardom. But to say that Shirley Temple, a five-year-old child, became a star entirely by luck is an injustice to her. She has been guided by her mother since she was a child, practicing various dance arts, to get to where she is now. And once someone reaches stardom, they must have the talent to maintain their position, and Shirley Temple's position is something that no other child can snatch away. Therefore, we can't help but admire the Fox Corporation's foresight in signing her to a long-term contract of seven years. During these seven years, she works six hours a day, filming every day. So, we can look forward to seeing more of this adorable little baby in the future.

She herself is a star, but she doesn't understand what a star is. Her parents also try their best to keep her from knowing, so she has no sense of self-importance. At this moment, she is playing with a girl companion on the set. Her mother calls out to her, "Shirley, come here." Shirley is playing too enthusiastically, she hears her mother calling her, and only replies, "Hello," and continues playing. Her mother then calls out again, "Shirley, come here." Shirley immediately puts down her toys and runs over. Regardless of whether she is a star, her mother is still her "Mommy." Her Mommy calls her to come, and she doesn't dare not come quickly. She comes, and she calls out, "Mommy, what is it?" She does whatever her mother tells her to do, and never disobeys her mother's wishes.

Every night, Shirley also has to memorize the lines for the next day's filming. She starts at eight o'clock, and goes to bed after she has memorized them. She gets up at seven o'clock every morning. She arrives at the studio before nine o'clock. Her face is so rosy and beautiful that it is even better than a vase. She also doesn't need makeup to go on camera, so the makeup time is very short. After working for six hours, she is exhausted when she gets home. She likes to rest her head on the pillow and meditate for a while. The people she thinks about are the head lighting technician Jilai, the star James Dunn, the third-class carpenter Tommy, the star Gary Cooper and the actress Carole Lombard, the assistant cameraman, the director Hathaway, Jenny Gaynor, and the children Marilyn, etc. In Shirley's little mind, there is absolutely no distinction of class. In her eyes, stars, lighting technicians, carpenters, directors, etc., are all equal friends, and they all love her with the same undivided attention.

Shirley Temple's temperament is naturally sunny. She doesn't know that there are things like disillusionment, tragedy, disappointment, and melancholy in the world. But she did have a big cry once. That day was the day after the actress Dorothy Dell died tragically in a car accident. Shirley was filming, and the camera was already ready. She suddenly heard the director Hathaway talking to someone about Miss Dell's tragic death. Shirley and Dell had co-starred in "Kidnapped Child Star," so when she heard this, she couldn't help but feel grief and burst into tears. No matter how others tried to comfort her, they couldn't persuade her. So the director simply let her cry, and ordered the camera to be turned on, and filmed segments of the scene while she was crying in Carole Lombard's arms. But her nature is closer to the side of happiness, so after she finished crying, she happily forgot the clouds of the day again.

Movie Review

Review of "The Lady Is Willing" 247

— Ling He

The Lady is Willing

丨Cathay丨

American films fully pay attention to the development of humor and wit, and now it has almost become a so-called "trend." I see this development in almost every film, regardless of the content of the work, which is determined to require serious and profound treatment, and the result is often that a large amount of slapstick destroys the heavy tone. Not long ago, "Whom the Gods Destroy" opened at the Great Light. In the latter part, it is undoubtedly a very profound tragedy, but in the first half, the playwright wanted to make it "funny" and "slapstick", and as a result, it became two separate existences before and after, with things that could not be unified in tone. Of course, the humorization of the first part made the profundity of the second part lose a lot. Similarly, we have seen many detective films that have also been relaxed and humorous, and besides "Mist Night", we can also cite many. If we classify "The Lady is Willing" as a detective film, then it is another comedic detective film.

In this film, the greatest achievement is undoubtedly the wit of the dialogue and the light and elegant rhythm. For the sake of humor, many funny characters have been added, and for the sake of lightness of tone, many interesting episodes that are not related to the content have been inserted.

In addition to some satire on ladies and entrepreneurs, the mockery of the three fools, describing them as very vulgar and funny characters, is an unconditional joke on the poor. Even Lee Bowman, who has always played sad tragedies, has become a humorous helper.

Yes, in terms of content, the humor here did not excessively lose the consistency of content and form. In other words, the characters contained in the story, except for the three fools, are all worth satirizing. However, strictly speaking, due to the random grabbing of chance materials, there is not much substantial content. But the playwright exaggerated this kind of material to the fullest extent, without weakening the characteristics of capitalist works at all, and became a work where form transcends content.

After the opening of "Puppet", someone actually said that "the form is not enough to express the content". In addition to illustrating that the film critics of the semi-colonial China are obsessed with the established form of American films, it is not enough to disprove the unity of content and form of "Puppet". Otherwise, they just don't understand enough. But on the other hand, we should strictly condemn American comedies that only exaggerate form without seeking content to be substantial and complete. Therefore, we have no way to give "The Lady is Willing" a higher evaluation, it is just a vulgar comedy.

Audience Opinions

My Review of "Red Chamber Spring Depths" 248

— Zhang Zigui

"Red Chamber Spring Depths" is a soft film worth watching, but it is a pity that it only caters to the psychology of a few people, and it is only used by the noble people of the leisure class as a tool for recreation.

However, "Red Chamber Spring Depths" also has its merits. The director is indeed a bit clever. For example, several inverted shots are very commendable, especially the large characters of "Wash Away National Humiliation" made of torches, which did add a lot of color. However, there are also a few places that should be brought up and discussed with the playwright. (1) Since Yu Qingfeng is a rational young artist and he already has an ideal lover Zhou Bilian, how can he not get rid of a romantic woman Luo Lan? At the same time, he was forced into adultery and marriage. (2) There are many gimmicks, and it is dragged into the formalized low-level taste. (3) After the wedding ceremony, he immediately went on a honeymoon trip "the night of the wedding". Maybe this is the playwright's new creation? Because I have never heard of it in custom.

As for the actors, they are working hard.

"Drunken Butterflies Among the Flowers" "All Flowers Gathering" Main Actors Mei Jiaoli and Huai De Arrive in Shanghai 249

After the movie star Betty Compson came to Shanghai, Mei Jiaoli and Huai De, the comedic dance stars of Fox Company, also arrived in Shanghai. In these years, the attraction of the oriental little Paris to Hollywood is more than once. The production of "The Good Earth" and the filming of "Oil Lamp" undoubtedly prove how the Westerners are paying attention to this Eastern nation! This time, Huai De came to Shanghai with her husband Eddie Tanant. The purpose is to investigate the East, and leave it for her new film to experience and contribute. At the same time, she was hired by the Paramount Ballroom to start performing tonight, performing her actions on the silver screen in a physical way for the entire Shanghai movie fans. Her husband is the dance director of Fox Company, and this time he also took the stage to perform, as a capable supporting role. With Compson in front and Huai De in the back, the people of Shanghai are really lucky!

About Fairy of the World 250

— Willow Catkin

After months of day and night efforts, and consuming the hard work of many people, the first Chinese sound and dance film "Fairy of the World" has finally been completed. It has been meeting with movie fans in Shanghai on the screen of Jincheng since last Saturday.

This is the first work of Mr. Du Danyue, who advocates fitness and beauty. The protagonist is Yuan Meiyun, and Ma Loufen, Bai Hong, Li Mingjian, Cang Yinqiu and many singers cooperated. Yuan Meiyun, who is gradually stepping into youth, since working hard on "The Roar of the Chinese Sea", due to the art of Meng Jin, has already brought her name to the peak of art. The general movie fans' expectations for this little girl's future are just like looking forward to the clouds in a severe drought. Now she has been pulled by Du Danyue to play the heroine of this dialogue sound film "Fairy of the World". With her innate acting talent and fluent Mandarin, she is of course able to do it happily.

There are also a few things that are worth special mention, that is, the clarity of the film's pronunciation is comparable to that of foreign films; and the beauty and magnificence of the picture are even more rare. At a time when foreign song and dance films are prevalent in the Chinese film market, it is not necessarily a blessing to have such a Chinese song and dance film for us to appreciate!

Movie Novel

Freedom Forever (Viva Villa) (17) 251

— Wen Ying

This is a tragic scene from the final days of the second Mexican Revolution. General Pasquel, the leader of the reactionaries, was besieged in the mountains of Chihuahua. Pancho Villa's army had suffered a setback, but Pasquel refused to press the attack, believing that his machine gun squads would ensure his ultimate victory. Thus, he miscalculated and was captured alive by Pancho. Pancho, sucking on an orange, walked up to the bound Pasquel. He said to Thomas, "Thomas, quickly untie him! A general is a general after all. This is truly absurd!" Thomas immediately untied Pasquel. Pasquel coldly thanked him with a snort. Pancho said, "It's nothing. Don't mention it. You think you're very brave, eh?" Pasquel said, "No need to be verbose. Just shoot me." Pancho laughed, "You speak well, much better than me. You know, I often think of you. Everyone in the world says Pancho Villa is a hero, a brave man. But in front of General Pasquel, I am just a man kneeling on the ground, crawling forward. I even begged, shouted, and cried, which was quite unsightly. Do you remember?" He threw the remains of the orange on the ground. Pasquel smiled slightly and said, "I remember very clearly." Pancho said, "I beg you to forgive me for everything I've done." Pasquel said, "If a person is afraid of death, he will do many strange things." Pancho said, "You're right. Afterwards, I asked myself many times: Pancho, are you really afraid of death? I said to myself: No! I tell you, maybe it's because of this. That little husband with the mustache. Love often makes a person afraid of death. That's philosophy, isn't it? Or you love someone, you also have a wife, children. Don't you want to see them again?" Pasquel sneered, "Do you want to hear me cry and shout? No, I'm sorry to disappoint you. I won't beg you. I won't cry either. I'm ready to be shot." Pancho laughed loudly, "Shoot? Who told you about shooting? Did you all talk about shooting?" As he spoke, he picked up a jar of honey from a long table and said to Pasquel, "General, this painting is not bad. From the same place as me. Would you like some?" Pasquel was looking down, and saw the orange remains that Pancho had just eaten and thrown on the ground, already swarming with white ants. When he saw the ants, he was as frightened as if he had seen a ghost. Beads of sweat as big as soybeans burst out from his forehead one by one and flowed down his face. Pancho slowly said, "They like honey, even more than oranges." As he spoke, he stuck two thick fingers into the honey jar, scooped up a large handful of honey, and dripping, walked up to Pasquel. Pasquel took a step back, his face turning green. Pancho reached out and shoved the honey-soaked fingers into his ears, smearing them all over Pasquel's face. Pasquel screamed wildly, "No! No! Not this way! You can't! Pancho! Don't do that! Let me say something! Pancho!" But Pancho nodded to his subordinates in Pasquel's direction, and several soldiers immediately dragged the pig-like general away. Pancho handed the jar of honey to Thomas and said, "Take this. Give him more. In his nose. In his ears. Anywhere. You know what to do." Thomas took the jar and retreated. Pasquel's miserable screams continued for half a day, slowly fading until they could no longer be heard. This is one example of Pancho Villa's inhumanity. Afterwards, he also ordered that all people of Spanish descent, regardless of age or gender, must leave Chihuahua within twenty-four hours, or they would all be shot. At this time, there was chaos, traffic was cut off, and there were no trains. The young and strong could still escape on foot. The old, young, weak, and disabled who were left behind would inevitably suffer a massacre. This was the result of the hatred accumulated from the various acts of tyranny during the Spanish rule of the Mexican natives, and Pancho's use of violence to replace violence only planted a bad seed for himself. (To be continued)
